  7-1-5, 7-1-7 and 8-1-4 of this code.
5-3B-8: DAMAGE TO STREETLAMPS:
No person shall deface, break, climb upon, meddle with, nor in any manner
injure any lamp or lamppost, or any fixture or attachment to any lamp or
lamppost, in any street or public place in the village. (1993 Code p. 38 §
402.1-33; amd. 2006 Code)
5-3B-9: DAMAGE TO TREES:
(Rep. by Ord. 2016-01-04, 1-4-2016)
5-3B-10: ENCROACHMENTS ON PUBLIC WAYS 1 :
   A.   Prohibited: No person shall make or cause to be made any structure,
enclosure, fence, cellar door, stairway, or building encroaching in whole or in
part upon any street, alley or sidewalk of the village. (1993 Code p. 41 §
402.1-46)
   B.   Failure To Remove: No person, being the owner of any structure,
enclosure, fence, cellar door, stairway, or building, which encroaches upon any
street, alley, or sidewalk, shall fail to remove the same within thirty (30)
days after written notice so to do. (1993 Code p. 41 § 402.1-47)
 
Notes
1 1. See also subsection
  4-1-1C of this code.
5-3B-11: TRESPASSES:
   A.   Trespasses Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or
corporation to commit a trespass within the village upon either public or
private property.
   B.   Specifically Enumerated Trespasses; Suppression: Without constituting
any limitation upon the provisions of subsection A of this section, any of the
following acts by any person, firm or corporation shall be deemed included
among those that constitute trespasses in violation of the provisions of
subsection A of this section, and appropriate action may be taken hereunder at
any time, or from time to time, to prevent or suppress any violation of this
section, the aforesaid enumerated acts so included, being as follows:
      1.   An entry upon the premises, or any part thereof, of another,
including any public property, in violation of a notice posted or exhibited at
the main entrance in said premises or at any point of approach or entry or in
violation of any notice, warning or protest given orally or in writing by any
owner or occupant thereof; or
      2.   The pursuit of a course of conduct or action incidental to the
making of an entry upon the land of another in violation of a notice posted or
exhibited at the main entrance to said premises or at any point of approach or
entry, or in violation of any notice, warning or protest given orally or in
writing by any owner or occupant thereof; or
      3.   A failure or refusal to depart from the premises of another in case
of being requested, either orally or in writing, to leave by any owner or
occupant thereof; or
      4.   An entry into or upon any vehicle, aircraft or watercraft made
without the consent of the person having the right to the possession or control
thereof, or a failure or refusal to leave any such vehicle, aircraft or
watercraft after being requested to leave by the person having such right.
(1993 Code p. 47 § 402.1-56; amd. 2006 Code)
5-3B-11-1: TRESPASSING TO DAMAGE PROPERTY:
No person shall wilfully, maliciously, or for mischief enter any orchard, yard,
garden, or enclosure of another and mutilate, injure, or destroy any tree,
shrub, vine, fruit or vegetable therein, nor take or carry away any fruit,
vegetable or flower therefrom without the consent of the owner or person in
charge of the same. (1993 Code p. 42 § 402.1-51)
5-3B-12: DAMAGE TO PUBLIC WATER SYSTEM:
No person shall wilfully injure or destroy any building, public well, pump or
other property belonging to the village. (1993 Code p. 42 § 402.1-52)
ARTICLE C.  OFFENSES AGAINST PEACE, SAFETY AND HEALTH
SECTION:
5-3C-1: Disturbing Assemblies
5-3C-2: Sports And Games Disturbing The Public
5-3C-3: Loitering
5-3C-4: Open Burning
5-3C-5: False Alarms
5-3C-6: Throwing Stones And Missiles
5-3C-7: Selling Tainted Food
5-3C-8: Amusements On Sundays
5-3C-9: Weapons, Explosives Discharge On Sundays
5-3C-10: Concealed Weapons
5-3C-11: Discharge Of Weapons; Fireworks; Bonfires
5-3C-1: DISTURBING ASSEMBLIES:
   A.   No person shall wilfully interrupt or disturb any school or other
assembly of people met for a lawful purpose. (1993 Code p. 34 § 402.1-8)
   B.   No person shall, by any menace, profane swearing, vulgar language, or
any disorderly or unusual conduct, interrupt or disturb any assembly of people
met for worship. (1993 Code p. 34 § 402.1-7; amd. 2006 Code)
5-3C-2: SPORTS AND GAMES DISTURBING THE PUBLIC:
No person shall, at any place in the village, throw stones, play ball, fly
kites or engage in any sport or exercise likely to frighten horses, injure
passengers, interfere with the passage of vehicles, or obstruct the business of
other persons. (1993 Code p. 36 § 402.1-20; amd. 2006 Code)
5-3C-3: LOITERING:
   A.   No person shall, with other persons, congregate about or upon any
stairway, doorway, window or in front of any business or dwelling house,
lecture room, church, or elsewhere, and by so doing, obstruct or interfere with
the free passage of persons entering, or occupying any such building or
premises, nor by his language, conversation or conduct, annoy, insult or
disturb persons passing along the streets or alleys, or occupying, residing or
doing business in any of said houses or places. (1993 Code p. 37a § 402.1-25)
   B.   No person shall loiter about the street corners or in the vicinity of
any church, schoolhouse, hotel, hall, store, shop, or other public place or
building, thereby obstructing any street or sidewalk, or interfering with
public convenience, or interrupting the owner or occupants of such places.
(1993 Code p. 43 § 402.1-54)
5-3C-4: OPEN BURNING 1 :
   A.   Hours; Burning On Public Ways; Supervision:
      1.   Provisions Are Additional: This subsection is in addition to any
county, state or federal regulation on burning in the village. (1993 Code p.
37b Ord., 1993; amd. 2006 Code)
      2.   Prohibited Hours: There shall be no burning in the village between
ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and eight o'clock (8:00) A.M.
      3.   Burning On Public Ways Prohibited: There shall be no burning on any
village roads or alleys.
      4.   Supervision: All fires must be under the supervision of a person
over the age of fourteen (14) years until the fire is extinguished.
      5.   Application For Exception: Any exception to this subsection must be
applied for in writing and approved by the park and trees committee chair or
the village board.
      6.   Penalty: Any violation of this subsection will subject the violator
to a fine between one hundred dollars ($100.00) and one thousand dollars
($1,000.00). (1993 Code p. 37b Ord., 1993)
   B.   Burning Near Buildings: No person shall burn or set fire to any
combustible matter within one hundred feet (100') of any shed, barn or building
without posting a person over the age of fourteen (14) years to guard the same
until such fire is entirely extinguished. (1993 Code p. 37a § 402.1-27; amd.
2006 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section 5-3C-11 of this article.
5-3C-5: FALSE ALARMS:
No person shall wilfully make a false alarm of fire by outcry or in any other
way nor shall any person make any false alarm of any kind calculated to disturb
the peace of the village. (1993 Code p. 38 § 402.1-34)
5-3C-6: THROWING STONES AND MISSILES:
No person shall throw or cast any stone or other missile upon or at any
building, tree or other public or private property, or upon any person in any
street, avenue, alley, land, public place, enclosed or unenclosed ground in the
village, nor shall any person aid or abet in the same. (1993 Code p. 39 §
402.1-38)
5-3C-7: SELLING TAINTED FOOD:
No person shall knowingly sell, or expose or offer for sale, any sick or
diseased animal, poultry or fish to be used or eaten for food, or the flesh of
any sick, diseased or otherwise unwholesome dead animal, poultry or fish, or
the flesh of any animal, fowl or fish not usually used or deemed wholesome for
food, or any other unsound or unwholesome provision or article of food or
drink. (1993 Code p. 40 § 402.1-39)
5-3C-8: AMUSEMENTS ON SUNDAYS:
No person or company shall keep open any place of business providing amusement
on Sunday. (1993 Code p. 42 § 402.1-50)
5-3C-9: WEAPONS, EXPLOSIVES DISCHARGE ON SUNDAYS:
No persons shall fire or discharge any cannon, gun, fowling piece, pistol or
firearms of any description without first obtaining permission of the president
or a member of the board of trustees, nor fire, explode, or set off any squibs,
crackers or anything containing powder, or other explosive substances on
Sunday. (1993 Code p. 34 § 402.1-6)
5-3C-10: CONCEALED WEAPONS:
No person, except a peace officer, shall carry or wear under his or her
clothing, or concealed about his or her person, any pistol, revolver, slug
shot, knuckles, bowie knife, dirk knife, dagger or any other dangerous or
deadly weapon without the written permission of the village president or board
of trustees. (1993 Code p. 36 § 402.1-22)
5-3C-11: DISCHARGE OF WEAPONS; FIREWORKS; BONFIRES:
No person shall, in any part of the village, fire or discharge any cannon, gun,
pistol or other firearms, nor set off, fire or explode any torpedo,
firecracker, fireball, rocket or other fireworks whatever, nor make or kindle
any bonfire 1 . However, the discharge of firearms, the setting off or
exploding of fireworks and the making of bonfires upon national holidays and in
the celebration of other public and general events, or the discharge of
firearms by the members of any military company when on parade and in
accordance with the command of the commanding officer, or by any village
officer or other person in the discharge of any legal duty or lawful act, when
the same may be done in such a manner as not to endanger the safety of any
person, or to the injury of any property, shall not be deemed a violation
hereof. (1993 Code p. 39 § 402.1-36)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section 5-3C-4 of this article.
ARTICLE D.  OFFENSES INVOLVING MORALS AND DECENCY
SECTION:
5-3D-1: Public Indecency
5-3D-2: Indecent Exposure; Nudity
5-3D-3: Obscene Publications And Articles
5-3D-4: Graffiti
5-3D-5: Prostitution Houses
5-3D-6: Gambling
5-3D-7: Sleight Of Hand Games
5-3D-8: Vagrants
5-3D-1: PUBLIC INDECENCY:
No person shall be guilty of open lewdness, disorderly conduct, or act of
public indecency tending to debauch the public morals. (1993 Code p. 33 §
402.1-5)
5-3D-2: INDECENT EXPOSURE; NUDITY:
No person, for the purpose of bathing or otherwise, shall appear in any public
place in a state of nudity nor make any indecent exposure of his or her person.
(1993 Code p. 34 § 402.1-9; amd. 2006 Code)
5-3D-3: OBSCENE PUBLICATIONS AND ARTICLES:
No person shall exhibit, sell or offer to sell, give away or offer to give away
any obscene and indecent book, pamphlet, paper, drawing, lithograph, engraving,
picture, daguerreotype, photograph, stereoscopic picture, mold, cast,
instrument, or article of indecent or immoral use. (1993 Code p. 34 § 402.1-10)
5-3D-4: GRAFFITI:
   A.   Definition: For the purpose of this section, "graffiti" is defined as
any sign, symbol, marking, drawing, name, initial, word, diagram, sketch,
picture, or letter, or combination thereof, placed without the express written
permission of the owner, upon the real or personal property of said owner.
   B.   Prohibited: It shall be unlawful to place graffiti upon the property of
another, whether publicly or privately owned, real or personal.
   C.   Placement With Owner's Permission: It shall be unlawful for an owner
and/or occupant of property which is in the public view to place or give
permission to place any graffiti on said property if such graffiti incites
violence or the furtherance or proliferation of gang activity by reference to
gang or criminal activity, depicts or expresses obscenity by referring to
sexual activity, or contains defamatory material about a public or private
person or group.
   D.   Removal Required: Upon notification by the village, the owner of
property upon which graffiti has been illegally placed shall remove the
graffiti within five (5) working days of the date of notification. Failure to
remove graffiti within the specified time shall cause summary abatement of the
nuisance, and cost therefor shall be assessed to the owner.
   E.   Compensation And Restitution: The owner of the property shall be
entitled to restitution and compensation for the direct cost incurred in the
repair and restoration of his property to its previous condition from any
person convicted of the offense listed in this section; provided, that the
property owner submits receipts or other evidence of the costs for the removal
or repair of the graffiti; and provided further, that the court enters an order
of restitution.
   F.   Responsibility Of Parent Or Guardian:
      1.   The parent or legal guardian of a juvenile who resides with such
parent or legal guardian is liable for actual damages for the wilful or
malicious acts of such juvenile which cause injury to a person or property. The
juvenile shall be deemed to have committed the offense with the knowledge,
consent, acquiescence and permission of the parent or legal guardian in
violation of this section.
      2.   The parent or legal guardian shall be liable for the fine and
requirement of restitution or reparation imposed by a court upon a juvenile
defendant for violation of this section.
      3.   The sanctions of this subsection shall apply after said parent or
legal guardian shall have received a written notice thereof, either by
certified or registered mail, return receipt requested, or by personal service
with a certificate of personal service returned, from the appropriate law
enforcement official prior to the institution of any judicial sanction or
penalty.
      4.   In any action brought pursuant to the provisions of this section,
the parent or legal guardian shall be made a party defendant. (2006 Code)
5-3D-5: PROSTITUTION HOUSES:
No person shall keep a house of ill fame or assignation or place for the
practice of prostitution or lewdness. No person shall patronize or be an inmate
of the same, nor let, own or be interested in any house, room or other premises
for any such purpose, nor keep a common, ill governed, disorderly house to the
encouragement of idleness, gaming, drinking, fornication or other misbehavior.
(1993 Code p. 34 § 402.1-11)
5-3D-6: GAMBLING:
   A.   Gambling Prohibited: No person shall play for money or other valuable
things at any game with cards, dice, checkers, or at billiards, or with any
other article, instrument or thing whatever, which may be used for the purpose
of playing or betting upon, or winning or losing money, or anything of value,
nor bet on any game others may be playing. (1993 Code p. 35 § 402.1-16)
   B.   Gambling Houses: No person shall keep a common gaming house, nor any
building, place, yard or garden by him or his agent, used and occupied, nor
procure or permit any persons to frequent or to come together to play for money
or other valuable thing at any game, nor keep or rent any such place for any
such purpose. (1993 Code p. 35 § 402.1-17)
5-3D-7: SLEIGHT OF HAND GAMES:
No person shall manage, use or practice any trick, sleight of hand, game or
device whatever with the intent of winning or procuring the property or money
of another person in inducing him to bet, loan, deposit, or stake money on
property upon the result of such trick or game. (1993 Code p. 35 § 402.1-18)
5-3D-8: VAGRANTS:
The following are deemed vagrants:
   A.   Possession Of Burglar Tools: Any person upon whom shall be found any
instrument or thing used for the commission of burglary or for picking locks or
pockets, and who shall fail to give a good account of the possession of the
same. (1993 Code p. 54 § 402.3-2)
   B.   Prostitutes: Any prostitute, courtesan, bawd or lewd person, or any
inmate of any bawdy house or house of prostitution or assignation, brothel or
house of bad repute who shall be wandering about the streets. (1993 Code p. 54
§ 402.3-3; amd. 2006 Code)
ARTICLE E.  OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC AUTHORITY
SECTION:
5-3E-1: Impersonating, Interfering With Officials
5-3E-2: Refusing To Aid In Arrest
5-3E-3: Aid In Escape
5-3E-1: IMPERSONATING, INTERFERING WITH OFFICIALS:
No person shall falsely represent himself to be an officer of the village, nor
without being duly authorized, exercise or attempt to exercise any of the
duties, functions or powers of a village officer, nor hinder, obstruct, resist,
or otherwise interfere with a village officer in the discharge of his official
duties, nor attempt to prevent any such officer from arresting, nor attempt to
rescue from such officer any person in his custody. (1993 Code p. 41 § 402.1-
43)
5-3E-2: REFUSING TO AID IN ARREST:
No person shall refuse to aid in the arrest of any offender when ordered to do
so by any law enforcement official, the village president, or any member of the
village board of trustees. (1993 Code p. 41 § 402.1-45)
5-3E-3: AID IN ESCAPE:
No person shall aid, abet, or encourage the rescue or escape from prison of any
person legally committed thereto, nor supply or attempt to supply any such
person with any weapon or with an implement or means of escape while in prison
or in the legal custody of any officer of the village. (1993 Code p. 42 §
402.1-48)
CHAPTER 4
ANIMAL CONTROL
SECTION:
5-4-1: Dogs
5-4-2: Livestock At Large
5-4-3: Offenses Involving Animals
5-4-4: Dangerous, Vicious Animals
5-4-1: DOGS:
   A.   Definition: The term "dog", as used in this section, shall include dogs
of the male and female sex. (1993 Code p. 91 § 405.1-7)
   B.   Registration Requirements:
      1.   Registration, Collar And Tag Required:
         a.   It shall be the duty of every person owning, keeping or harboring
any dog in the village, annually, to register the same with the county
treasurer and to put and keep on the neck of such dog a collar of leather,
metal, or plastic, having attached thereto the registration tag provided by the
registration herein mentioned. Any dog not having a county license affixed to
the collar shall be impounded by the county dog catcher. (1993 Code p. 90 §
405.1-2)
         b.   No owner or keeper of any dog shall allow or permit such dog to
be within the limits of the village unless the same shall have been registered
as herein required, and unless such a dog shall be provided with such collar,
having attached thereto the check or tag herein mentioned, nor shall any owner
or keeper of any dog permit or allow the same to wear any tag or check other
than that issued for said dog or a tag identical to the one issued. (1993 Code
p. 90 § 405.1-3)
      2.   Unauthorized Removal Of Tag Prohibited: No person shall remove or
cause to be removed the collar, check or tag from any registered dog without
the consent of the owner or keeper thereof. (1993 Code p. 90 § 405.1-4; amd.
2006 Code)
      3.   Failure To Wear Tag; Nuisance Declared; Impoundment: Any dog not
registered as herein required or not provided with a collar having attached
thereto the check or tag as herein provided is hereby declared a nuisance and
shall be taken up by the appropriate law enforcement official and placed in the
village or county pound provided for dogs. (1993 Code p. 90 § 405.1-5)
   C.   Running At Large Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any person,
association or corporation to permit any dog owned by such person, association
or corporation to run at large in the village. (1993 Code p. 90 § 405.1-1)
   D.   Leash And Confinement Requirements: All owner(s) or persons in charge
or having custody of any dog within the village shall at all times keep said
dog on a leash and attended by a person of sufficient ability to control the
same, or shall keep said dog fastened to a secure object of sufficient weight
to prevent movement of said animal beyond the limits of the leash or chain, or
shall cause said animal to be confined to a pen or building constructed of
sufficient materials and size to prevent the freedom of said animal. Any
confinement of such animal shall be on the premises owned and controlled by the
owner of said dog or the person in charge of the care and control of said dog.
(1993 Code p. 91 § 405.1-9; amd. 2006 Code)
   E.   Impoundment And Redemption Provisions:
      1.   Authority To Impound: The county animal control warden appointed by
the county board of supervisors shall have the authority to seize any animal
described in this section which is in violation of this section.
      2.   Impoundment Costs; Authority To Destroy Dog: The county animal
control officer shall be authorized to charge the owner of any dog which is
permitted to run at large in violation of this section the sum of two dollars
($2.00) per day for feed and board of said dog and shall be permitted to
destroy said dog if not claimed within seven (7) days after seizure of said
dog. (1993 Code p. 91 § 405.1-10)
      3.   Reclamation, Destruction Of Dogs: Any dog may be released from the
pound by the owner upon proof of ownership at any time within seven (7) days
from the time such dog shall have been impounded, upon the production of a
certificate of registry in force for such dog and upon the payment of all pound
fees. All dogs not so released within such time shall be destroyed by the
appropriate law enforcement official or the county dog catcher or county animal
control officer as the case may be. (1993 Code p. 90 § 405.1-6; p. 91 § 405.1-
10)
   F.   Noisy Dogs 1 : No person shall keep or harbor any dog in the village
which, by loud and frequent or habitual barking, howling, or yelling, shall
annoy or disturb any neighborhood. (1993 Code p. 91 § 405.1-8)
   G.   Penalties: Any person, firm, partnership, association or corporation
violating the provisions of this section shall be fined not less than the
following sums: twenty five dollars ($25.00) for the first offense, fifty
dollars ($50.00) for the second offense within the period of twelve (12)
months, and seventy five dollars ($75.00) for the third offense occurring
within twelve (12) months. (1993 Code p. 91 § 405.1-10)
 
Notes
1 1. See also subsection
  5-4-3C of this chapter.
5-4-2: LIVESTOCK AT LARGE:
   A.   Prohibited: No person shall knowingly or wilfully permit his horses,
mules, sheep, asses, hogs, or cattle to run at large upon any street, lane,
alley, or public grounds of the village. (1993 Code p. 42 § 402.1-49; amd. 2006
Code)
   B.   Violation; Penalty: Violation of this section shall be deemed a
misdemeanor which, if severally or jointly committed by any person or
corporation within the territorial jurisdiction of the village, shall subject
the offender, severally, to a penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (1993 Code p. 33 § 402.1; amd. 2006 Code)
5-4-3: OFFENSES INVOLVING ANIMALS:
   A.   Cruelty: No person shall overload, cruelly beat, ill treat, torture,
mutilate or cruelly kill any animal, or cause or knowingly allow the same to be
done. (1993 Code p. 35 § 402.1-13)
   B.   Animal Fights: No person shall instigate, cause or procure any
dogfight, prizefight, cockfight, or any public or private fighting. (1993 Code
p. 35 § 402.1-14)
   C.   Noisy Animals 1 :
      1.   No person shall in the village keep any dog or other animal shut or
tied up in any yard, house or other place which, by barking, howling or by
other noises, shall disturb the peace and quiet of any person. (1993 Code p.
37a § 402.1-26; amd. 2006 Code)
      2.   No person shall suffer any animal belonging to him to wear a bell to
the annoyance of any other person. (1993 Code p. 39 § 402.1-35)
   D.   Indecent Exhibition Of Animals: No person shall instigate, cause or
procure, or in any manner assist in any indecent exhibition of any animal, nor
exhibit or perform any indecent, immoral, or lewd play or show or
representation of any kind involving animals. (1993 Code p. 34 § 402.1-12; amd.
2006 Code)
   E.   Dead Animals To Be Buried: No person, being the owner or keeper of any
dead animal, shall allow said dead animal to remain within the territorial
jurisdiction of the village without being buried. (1993 Code p. 36 § 402.1-21;
amd. 2006 Code)
   F.   Penalty: Violation of any provision of this section shall be deemed a
misdemeanor which, if severally or jointly committed by any person or
corporation within the territorial jurisdiction of the village, shall subject
the offender, severally, to a penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (1993 Code p. 33 § 402.1; amd. 2006 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See also subsection
  5-4-1F of this chapter.
5-4-4: DANGEROUS, VICIOUS ANIMALS:
   A.   Definition:
      1.   As used in this section, a "dangerous animal" or "vicious animal"
is:
         a.   Any individual animal that, when unprovoked, inflicts bites and
attacks a human being or other animal either on public or private property.
         b.   Any individual animal with a propensity, tendency or disposition
to attack without provocation, to cause injury or to otherwise do any act that
might endanger the safety of human beings, domestic animals or any other
property of another, including, but not limited to, a disposition to mischief
or fierceness which might lead to attack of the foregoing.
         c.   Any individual animal which attacks a human being or domestic
animal without provocation, whether in play, anger or outbreak of untrained
nature.
      2.   No animal shall be deemed "vicious" if it bites, attacks or menaces
a trespasser on the property of its owner, or harms or menaces anyone who has
tormented or abused it, or is a professionally trained animal for law
enforcement or guard duties.
   B.   Dangerous, Vicious Animals Prohibited:
      1.   No person shall keep any vicious animal anywhere in the village.
      2.   It shall be unlawful to permit any vicious animal of any kind to run
at large within the village.
   C.   Authority To Kill:
      1.   The village law enforcement official or any authorized village
official or employee is authorized to kill any dangerous animal of any kind
when it is necessary for the protection of any person or property.
      2.   It shall be lawful for the village law enforcement official or other
authorized village official or employee to kill any vicious animal at large
within the limits of the village which cannot be safely taken up and impounded.
   D.   Responsibility Of Landlord:
      1.   No landlord or landlord's agent shall knowingly permit any tenant to
move a vicious animal into any building or premises owned or controlled by such
landlord or agent.
      2.   No landlord or landlord's agent shall permit any person to keep any
vicious animal in any building or premises owned or controlled by such landlord
or agent.
      3.   Any landlord or agent learning of any vicious animal in any building
or premises owned or controlled by such landlord or agent shall notify the
person having such animal to remove the animal from the village immediately.
   E.   Application And Effect Of Provisions:
      1.   Police Dogs: It is not the intent of this section to prohibit the
village law enforcement official from using any trained dog that may attack
upon command; provided, that each such dog must be in the presence of its
handler or confined in accordance with village policy at all times.
      2.   Impoundment: This section shall not prohibit the temporary
impoundment in a public pound of any animal.
      3.   Rabies Suspects: This section shall not prohibit the holding of any
vicious animal suspected of rabies or any vicious animal that has bitten a
person; provided, that such vicious animal may be held only in a public pound
or in a secure place operated or immediately supervised by a licensed
veterinarian.
   F.   Enforcement And Penalty:
      1.   Nuisance Declared: Any violation of this section is hereby declared
to be a nuisance.
      2.   Remedies: In addition to other relief provided by this section, the
village attorney may apply to a court of competent jurisdiction for any
injunction to prohibit the continuation of any violation of this section. Such
application for relief may include the seeking of a temporary restraining
order, temporary injunction or permanent injunction.
      3.   Responsibility For Expenses: The owner of such animal is responsible
for any expenses incurred in connection with the impoundment, supervision and
examination by a veterinarian, inoculations, and if necessary, preparation of
the carcass for laboratory examinations, and fee for the laboratory examination
and disposal of the animal.
      4.   Penalty: Any person violating any provision of this section shall be
subject to penalty of not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor more than one
hundred dollars ($100.00) for each offense, and a separate offense shall be
deemed committed for each day during or on which a violation occurs or
continues. (2006 Code)
CHAPTER 5
EXPLOSIVE, FLAMMABLE MATERIALS
SECTION:
5-5-1: Definitions
5-5-2: Quantity Of Explosives
5-5-3: Storage Of Explosives
5-5-4: Anhydrous Ammonia
5-5-5: Petroleum Tanks
5-5-6: Transporting Explosive, Flammable Materials
5-5-7: Penalty
5-5-1: DEFINITIONS:
   EXPLOSIVE: Shall include any chemical compound and any mechanical mixture
that is commonly used or intended for the purpose of producing an explosion and
containing any oxidizing or combustible units or other ingredients in such
proportions, quantities or packing that an ignition by fire, friction,
concussion, percussion or detonation of any part of the compounds or mixtures
may cause sudden generation of highly heated gases so that the resultant
gaseous pressures are capable of producing destructive effects. The term
"explosive" shall include mixed ammunition, fireworks and other manufactured
articles which contain "explosives" as defined herein, but not fuses so
constructed and packed as to render explosion impossible.
   FLAMMABLE LIQUID: Shall include gasoline, naphtha, benzine, kerosene, motor
fuel oil or any other liquid having a flashpoint at seventy degrees Fahrenheit
(70°F) or below, by the closed cup test method.
   VEHICLE: Shall include any vehicle, trailer or semitrailer propelled by
mechanical, motor or muscular power, other than a railroad car on rails. (1993
Code p. 84 § 404.7-6)
5-5-2: QUANTITY OF EXPLOSIVES:
No storekeeper or shopkeeper or other person shall be allowed to have or keep
at any one time, in any building, house shop, store, cellar or warehouse within
the village, more than fifty (50) pounds of powder, nor more than twenty (20)
pounds of dynamite, nitroglycerine or other powerful explosives without a
special permit from the board of trustees, to be entered upon the journal of
their proceedings. (1993 Code p. 84 § 404.7-1)
5-5-3: STORAGE OF EXPLOSIVES:
All dynamite, nitroglycerine or other powerful explosives shall be kept in an
outbuilding of iron. All powder within the village, when kept in any quantity
exceeding one pound, shall be kept in closed tin or metallic canisters and in
some safe place secure from fire or anything which may ignite the same, and
proper care shall in all cases be taken to prevent accidents arising therefrom.
(1993 Code p. 84 § 404.7-2)
5-5-4: ANHYDROUS AMMONIA:
   A.   Storage Requirements: It shall be the duty of every person, association
or corporation in the village owning, operating or maintaining storage
facilities for anhydrous ammonia to maintain, operate and handle said anhydrous
ammonia and storage facilities for anhydrous ammonia according to the standards
for the storage and handling of anhydrous ammonia prepared by the engineering
standards and standardization committee of the Agricultural Ammonia Institute
as revised June 22, 1953, which said standards are hereby adopted by reference
as an ordinance of the village as if fully recited herein. (1993 Code p. 84 §
404.7-4)
   B.   Location Of Tanks:
      1.   Tanks for the storage and handling of anhydrous ammonia shall be
located outside of buildings other than those expressly constructed for this
purpose.
      2.   Permanent storage shall be located outside of densely populated
areas and shall be located only upon a site approved by the village president
and board of trustees and only upon a site not less than fifty feet (50') from
the property line which may be built upon or from a source of drinking water,
and not less than four hundred feet (400') from any school, hospital, or other
place of public assembly. (1993 Code p. 84 § 404.7-5)
5-5-5: PETROLEUM TANKS:
   A.   Location Prohibitions For Aboveground Tanks: It shall be unlawful for
any person, corporation or association to keep or permit to be kept on his or
its premises or on any demised premises or on any public street, alley or
highway any gasoline storage facility which shall be erected above the ground
level within the following described area within the village:
Blocks One (1) through Twenty-nine (29) inclusive, of the Original Town of
Stronghurst; Blocks Forty (40) through Forty-nine (49) inclusive, of the Second
Addition to the Village of Stronghurst; Blocks Thirty-one (31) through Thirty-
nine (39) inclusive, of the First Addition to the Village of Stronghurst;
Blocks Two (2), Three (3), Four (4), Seven (7), Eight (8), Eleven (11) and
Twelve (12) in Thompson's Addition to the Village of Stronghurst; all of
Dixson's Addition to the Village of Stronghurst; all of Main's Addition to the
Village of Stronghurst; an area bounded by the public road on the North side of
Section  Twenty-five (25) in Stronghurst Township, and the East right of way
line of Cooper Street in the Village of Stronghurst if extended by the two said
aforementioned streets; and an area described as bounded by the public road on
the North side of said Section Twenty-Five (25), the east line of the Original
Town Plat of the Village of Stronghurst and the North side of Maple Street in
the Village of Stronghurst; and an area described as bounded on the North by
the public road on the North side of said Section Twenty-Five (25), the East
line of Chicago Avenue, the North line of the Atchison, Topeka and Santa Fe
Railway right of way and the West right of way line of State Bond Issue Route
94.
(1993 Code p. 71 § 403.5-1)
   B.   Existing Tanks: This section shall in no way prohibit such gasoline
storage facilities as are now used within the village by service stations or
bulk distribution plants as are now located within the village. (1993 Code p.
71 § 403.5-3)
5-5-6: TRANSPORTING EXPLOSIVE, FLAMMABLE MATERIALS:
   A.   Explosives:
      1.   It shall be unlawful to operate any vehicle containing explosives on
any street in the village except in compliance with the following rules:
         a.   No such vehicle shall be so operated unless it is marked, loaded
and equipped in full compliance with all the laws of the state relating
thereto.
         b.   No trailer shall be used for the conveyance of explosives in the
village, but "semitrailers", as defined by statute, may be so used.
         c.   No vehicle carrying explosives shall be parked or permitted to
stand anywhere in the village longer than is necessary to make a lawful
delivery; provided, that the standing of such vehicle made necessary by
mechanical trouble, traffic conditions, accident or in obedience to the
direction of an appropriate law enforcement official or traffic signals shall
not be considered a violation of this subsection A1. (1993 Code p. 88 § 404.7-
8)
      2.   It shall be unlawful to operate any vehicle carrying explosives on
any street in the village that is so slippery because of ice, snow or from any
other cause as to be unsafe for driving. (1993 Code p. 88 § 404.7-9)
   B.   Warning Devices: Whenever a vehicle carrying explosives or flammable
liquids is disabled in the village, warning flags or lights shall be placed as
required by statute, and it shall be unlawful to permit any vehicle carrying
explosives to remain unattended at any such time. (1993 Code p. 88 § 404.7-10;
amd. 2006 Code)
   C.   Work Causing Sparks Or Fire:
      1.   No work involving danger of sparks, fire, friction or concussion
which might cause an explosion shall be performed on any vehicle carrying
explosives, and no such vehicle shall be brought into or kept in any garage in
the village; nor shall such vehicle carrying explosives be permitted to remain
anywhere in the village under any circumstances for a period of more than five
(5) hours.
      2.   No work which involves or is apt to produce sparks or fire shall be
performed on any vehicle tank which has been used in the transportation of any
flammable liquids until all flammable vapors have been effectively cleared from
such tank. (1993 Code p. 88 § 404.7-10)
   D.   Railroad Crossings: No vehicle containing explosives or flammable
liquids shall be driven or propelled across any railroad track unless it is
first brought to a full stop within not less than fifteen (15) nor more than
fifty feet (50') therefrom. (1993 Code p. 89 § 404.7-13; amd. 2006 Code)
   E.   Transporting Nitroglycerine Prohibited: It shall be unlawful to
transport liquid nitroglycerine by "vehicle", as defined in section
5-5-1 of this chapter, anywhere in the village. (1993 Code p. 88 § 404.7-11)
   F.   Exemptions From Provisions: The provisions of this section relating to
explosives shall not apply to the transportation of nitroglycerine in capsule
form, or in solution, in quantities not exceeding a total of one ounce
avoirdupois in weight; nor to the lawful transportation of properly packed
ammunition in quantities not exceeding twenty five (25) pounds in weight; nor
to the transportation of ammunition by the armed forces of the United States of
America or the state of Illinois or by law enforcement officials or other
conservators of the peace in the performance of their duties. (1993 Code p. 88
§ 404.7-12)
5-5-7: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be fined as provided
in section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense, and a separate offense shall be deemed
committed on each day during or on which a violation occurs or continues. (2006
Code)
CHAPTER 6
DRUGS AND DRUG PARAPHERNALIA
SECTION:
5-6-1: Definitions
5-6-2: Sale, Delivery To/Or Possession Of Drug Paraphernalia
5-6-3: Exceptions
5-6-4: Possession, Use Or Delivery Of Cannabis
5-6-5: Seizure And Forfeiture
5-6-6: Penalty
5-6-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise requires:
   CANNABIS: As defined in section 3 of the state of Illinois, cannabis control
act, for the purpose of this chapter.
   CONTROLLED SUBSTANCE: As defined in section 102 of the state of Illinois,
Illinois controlled substances act, for the purpose of this chapter.
   DELIVER OR DELIVERY: The actual, constructive or attempted transfer of
possession, with or without consideration, whether or not there is an agency
relationship.
   DRUG PARAPHERNALIA: All equipment, products and materials of any kind, other
than methamphetamine manufacturing materials as defined in section 10 of the
state of Illinois methamphetamine control and community protection act, which
are intended to be used unlawfully in planting, propagating, cultivating,
growing, harvesting, manufacturing, compounding, converting, producing,
processing, preparing, testing, analyzing, packaging, repackaging, storing,
containing, concealing, injecting, ingesting, inhaling or otherwise introducing
into the human body cannabis or a controlled substance in violation of the
Illinois cannabis control act or the Illinois controlled substances act. Drug
paraphernalia includes, but is not limited to:
   A.   Kits intended to be used unlawfully in manufacturing, compounding,
converting, producing, processing or preparing cannabis or a controlled
substance;
   B.   Isomerization devices intended to be used unlawfully in increasing the
potency of any species of plant which is cannabis or a controlled substance;
   C.   Testing equipment intended to be used unlawfully in a private home for
identifying or in analyzing the strength, effectiveness or purity of cannabis
or controlled substances;
   D.   Diluents and adulterants intended to be used unlawfully for cutting
cannabis or a controlled substance by private persons;
   E.   Objects primarily intended to be used unlawfully in ingesting,
inhaling, or otherwise introducing cannabis, cocaine, hashish, or hashish oil
into the human body including, where applicable, the following items:
      1.   Water pipes;
      2.   Carburetion tubes and devices;
      3.   Smoking and carburetion masks;
      4.   Miniature cocaine spoons and cocaine vials;
      5.   Carburetor pipes;
      6.   Electric pipes;
      7.   Air driven pipes;
      8.   Chillums;
      9.   Bongs;
      10.   Ice pipes or chillers;
   F.   Any item whose purpose as announced or described by the seller or
possessor is for use in violation of this section. (Ord. 2010-07-05, 7-5-2010)
5-6-2: SALE, DELIVERY TO/OR POSSESSION OF DRUG PARAPHERNALIA:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person to knowingly possess an item of
drug paraphernalia with the intent to use it in ingesting, inhaling or
otherwise introducing cannabis or a controlled substance into the human body,
or for the purpose of preparing cannabis or a controlled substance for that
use. The provisions of this subsection shall not apply to persons legally
authorized to possess hypodermic syringes or needles under the state of
Illinois hypodermic syringes and needles act.
In determining intent under this section the court, administrative hearing
officer or other trier of fact may take into consideration the proximity of the
cannabis or controlled substance to the drug paraphernalia or the presence of
cannabis or controlled substance on or in the drug paraphernalia.
   B.   It shall be unlawful for any person to offer for sale, sell, or deliver
for any commercial consideration any item of drug paraphernalia.
   C.   Any store, place, or premises from which or in which any item of drug
paraphernalia is kept for sale, offered for sale, sold, or delivered for any
commercial consideration is hereby declared to be a public nuisance.
The village attorney, upon direction of the village president and board of
trustees, at the recommendation of the chief of police, may commence an action
in the circuit court of Henderson County to abate the public nuisance as
described herein as outlined under section
4-1-2, "Penalties; Abatement Procedures", of this code. (Ord. 2010-07-05, 7-5-
2010)
5-6-3: EXCEPTIONS:
This chapter shall not apply to:
   A.   Items marketed for use in the preparation, compounding, packaging,
labeling, or other use of cannabis or a controlled substance as an incident to
lawful research, teaching, or chemical analysis and not for sale; or
   B.   Items marketed for, or historically and customarily used in connection
with the planting, propagating, cultivating, growing, harvesting,
manufacturing, compounding, converting, producing, processing, preparing,
testing, analyzing, packaging, repackaging, storing, containing, concealing,
injecting, ingesting, or inhaling of tobacco or any other lawful substance.
   C.   Items exempt under this section shall include, but are not limited to,
garden hoes, rakes, sickles, baggies, tobacco pipes, and cigarette rolling
papers.
   D.   Items listed in the definition of "drug paraphernalia" in section
5-6-1 of this chapter which are marketed for decorative purposes, when such
items have been rendered completely inoperable or incapable of being used for
any illicit purpose prohibited by this section, state or federal law.
   E.   In determining whether or not a particular item is exempt under this
section, the trier of fact should consider, in addition to all other logically
relevant factors, the following:
      1.   The general, usual, customary, and historical use to which the item
involved has been put;
      2.   Expert evidence concerning the ordinary or customary use of the item
and the effect of any peculiarity in the design or engineering of the device
upon its functioning;
      3.   Any written instructions accompanying the delivery of the item
concerning the purposes or uses to which the item can or may be put;
      4.   Any oral instructions provided by the seller of the item at the time
and place of sale or commercial delivery;
      5.   Any national or local advertising, concerning the design, purpose or
use of the item involved, and the entire context in which such advertising
occurs;
      6.   The manner, place and circumstances in which the item was displayed
for sale, as well as any item or items displayed for sale or otherwise
exhibited upon the premises where the sale was made;
      7.   Whether the owner or anyone in control of the object is a legitimate
supplier of like or related items to the community, such as a licensed
distributor or dealer of tobacco products;
      8.   The existence and scope of legitimate uses for the object in the
community;
      9.   All reasonable and common sense inferences shall be drawn in favor
of the legitimacy of any transaction or item suspect under the provisions of
this section. (Ord. 2010-07-05, 7-5-2010)
5-6-4: POSSESSION, USE OR DELIVERY OF CANNABIS:
It shall be unlawful for any person knowingly to possess, use or deliver any
substance containing cannabis. This section shall apply only to possession, use
or delivery of such substance in an amount not exceeding thirty grams (30 g).
(Ord. 2010-07-05, 7-5-2010)
5-6-5: SEIZURE AND FORFEITURE:
Any drug paraphernalia or substance containing cannabis that is the subject of
a violation of this chapter shall be subject to seizure and subject to
forfeiture upon a finding of guilty or finding of liable of any person for a
violation of this chapter. Upon appropriate order of court or administrative
hearing officer, said drug paraphernalia and/or substance containing cannabis
shall be destroyed. (Ord. 2010-07-05, 7-5-2010)
5-6-6: PENALTY:
Any person found to have violated the provisions of this chapter shall be fined
in an amount not less than two hundred dollars ($200.00) nor more than seven
hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) for each offense as outlined under
title 1, chapter 4, "General Penalty", of this code. (Ord. 2010-07-05, 7-5-
2010)
CHAPTER 7
EMERGENCY SERVICES AND DISASTER OPERATIONS
SECTION:
5-7-1: Definitions
5-7-2: Establishment Of The Emergency Services And Disaster Agency (ESDA)
5-7-3: ESDA Director
5-7-4: ESDA General Staff
5-7-5: Reserved
5-7-6: Reserved
5-7-7: Reserved
5-7-8: ESDA Functions
5-7-9: Service As Mobile Support Team
5-7-10: Agreements With Other Political Subdivisions
5-7-11: Emergency Action
5-7-12: Compensation
5-7-13: Reimbursement By State
5-7-14: Purchase And Expenditures
5-7-15: Local Disaster Emergencies
5-7-16: Emergency Operations Center
5-7-1: DEFINITIONS:
   EOC: ESDA emergency operations center.
   ESDA: Unless otherwise noted, "Stronghurst emergency services and disaster
agency".
   GENERAL STAFF: Organizational body of ESDA responsible for the planning and
operation of the village of Stronghurst's disaster preparedness plan.
   IEMA: Illinois emergency management agency.
   NIMS: National incident management system. (Ord. 2011-03-07, 3-7-2011)
5-7-2: ESTABLISHMENT OF THE EMERGENCY SERVICES AND DISASTER AGENCY (ESDA):
   A.   The village board of Stronghurst hereby creates the village of
Stronghurst emergency services and disaster agency to prevent, minimize,
repair, and alleviate injury or damage resulting from disaster(s) caused by an
enemy attack, sabotage, or other hostile action or from natural or manmade
disaster(s), in accordance with the Illinois emergency services and disaster
agency act of 1988 or as directed by Illinois homeland security or Illinois
emergency management agency.
   B.   The ESDA shall consist of the director and members comprising the
general staff. (Ord. 2011-03-07, 3-7-2011)
5-7-3: ESDA DIRECTOR:
   A.   The Stronghurst chief of police shall also serve as the ESDA director
unless as appointed by the village president with the confirmation by the
village board of trustees, and shall serve until removed by the village
president.
   B.   The director shall serve as the point of contact for outside agencies
and is responsible for maintaining required documentation or records including,
but not limited to, requirements as outlined under the national incident
management system (NIMS).
   C.   The director shall work closely with the general staff with planning,
coordination, and operation of the village of Stronghurst disaster preparedness
plan as well as assist the Henderson County emergency management coordinator
with coordinating county, state and/or federal responders.
   D.   The director shall actively seek and apply for state and federal grants
or other sources funding for the purchase of equipment, training or other
operational needs of ESDA.
   E.   In the event of the absence, resignation, death, or inability to serve
as the director, the deputy chief of police shall assume command and
responsibility of ESDA or as appointed by the village president until a new
such director is appointed and confirmed as directed in this section. (Ord.
2011-03-07, 3-7-2011)
5-7-4: ESDA GENERAL STAFF:
   A.   The general staff shall operate under the "unified command structure"
as outlined under NIMS with each general staff member responsible for response
planning and operation of the Stronghurst disaster preparedness plan.
   B.   It is at the discretion of the representing body to appoint their
representatives to the ESDA general staff.
   C.   The ESDA general staff shall be comprised of, but not limited to, the
following members or representatives from the following local community
services or agencies:
      1.   Stronghurst village board president.
      2.   Director of ESDA.
      3.   Village services:
         a.   ESDA coordinator.
         b.   Public works.
         c.   Records-finance.
      4.   Stronghurst police department.
      5.   MST fire department.
      6.   Henderson County emergency medical services.
      7.   Henderson County emergency management coordinator.
   D.   Any member of the ESDA general staff has the authority to activate in
whole or in part, the Stronghurst disaster preparedness plan or operation of
the ESDA emergency operations center (EOC). If time and response allows, the
ESDA director shall be notified prior to activation, otherwise the ESDA
director shall be notified as soon as possible. (Ord. 2011-03-07, 3-7-2011)
5-7-5: RESERVED:
(Ord. 2011-03-07, 3-7-2011)
5-7-6: RESERVED:
(Ord. 2011-03-07, 3-7-2011)
5-7-7: RESERVED:
(Ord. 2011-03-07, 3-7-2011)
5-7-8: ESDA FUNCTIONS:
The ESDA shall perform such emergency services and disaster agency functions
with the village of Stronghurst as shall be prescribed in and by the county or
state emergency management plan and program prepared by the governor and such
orders, rules, and regulations as may be promulgated by the governor, and in
addition shall perform such duties outside the corporate limits as may be
required pursuant to any mutual aid agreement with any other political
subdivision or municipality, entered into as provided in the Illinois emergency
services and disaster agency act of 1988 1 . (Ord. 2011-03-07, 3-7-2011)
 
Notes
1 1. 20 ILCS 3305/1 et seq.
5-7-9: SERVICE AS MOBILE SUPPORT TEAM:
   A.   Any or all members of the ESDA may be designated as members of a mobile
support team created by the governor or the director of IEMA as provided by
law.
   B.   The leader of such mobile support team shall be designated by the
director of IEMA.
   C.   Any member of the mobile support team who is a village employee or
officer while serving on duty by the governor, or the director of IEMA, shall
receive compensation and have the powers, duties, rights, privileges and
immunities incident to such employment or office. Any such member who is not a
paid employee or officer of the village, while so serving, shall receive from
the state compensation as provided by law. (Ord. 2011-03-07, 3-7-2011)
5-7-10: AGREEMENTS WITH OTHER POLITICAL SUBDIVISIONS:
The ESDA director may negotiate mutual aid agreements with other political
subdivisions or municipalities of the state, but no such agreement shall be
effective until it has been approved by the village board of trustees. (Ord.
2011-03-07, 3-7-2011)
5-7-11: EMERGENCY ACTION:
If the governor proclaims that a disaster emergency exists in an actual enemy
attack upon the United States or the occurrence within the state or a major
disaster resulting from enemy sabotage or other hostile action or from manmade
or natural disaster, it shall be the duty of the ESDA to cooperate fully with
IEMA and with the governor in the exercise of emergency powers as provided by
law. (Ord. 2011-03-07, 3-7-2011)
5-7-12: COMPENSATION:
Members of the ESDA who are paid employees or officers of the village, if
called for training by the director of IEMA, shall receive for the time spent
in such training the same rate of pay as is attached to the position held.
Members who are not such village employees or officers shall receive for such
training time such compensation as may be established by the village board of
trustees. (Ord. 2011-03-07, 3-7-2011)
5-7-13: REIMBURSEMENT BY STATE:
The state treasurer may receive and allocate to the appropriate fund any
reimbursement by the state to the village for expenses incident to training
members of the ESDA as prescribed by the director of the Illinois emergency
management agency, compensation for the services and expenses of members of a
mobile support team while serving outside the village in response to a call by
the governor or the director of IEMA, as provided by law, and any other
reimbursement made by the state incident to ESDA activities as provided by law.
(Ord. 2011-03-07, 3-7-2011)
5-7-14: PURCHASE AND EXPENDITURES:
   A.   The village board of trustees may, on recommendation of the village
ESDA director, authorize any purchase or contract necessary to place the
village in a position to combat effectively any disaster resulting from the
explosion of any nuclear or other bomb or missile, and to protect the public
health and safety, protect property, and provide emergency assistance to
victims in the case of such disaster or from manmade or natural disaster.
   B.   In the event of enemy caused or other disaster, the village board
president is authorized, on behalf of the village to procure such services,
supplies, equipment, or material as may be necessary for such purposes, in view
of the exigency, without regard to the statutory procedures or formalities
normally prescribed by law pertaining to village contracts or obligations, such
as authorized by the state emergency services and disaster agency act of 1988,
provided that if the village board of trustees meets at such time he shall act
subject to the directions and restrictions imposed by that body. (Ord. 2011-03-
07, 3-7-2011)
5-7-15: LOCAL DISASTER EMERGENCIES:
   A.   A local disaster emergency may be declared only by the principal
executive officer of a political subdivision, member of the ESDA general staff
or his/her interim emergency successor, as provided in section 7 of the
emergency interim executive succession act. It shall not be continued or
renewed for a period in excess of seven (7) days except by or the consent of
the village board of trustees. Any order or proclamation declaring, continuing,
or terminating a local disaster emergency shall be given prompt and general
publicity and shall be filed promptly with the village clerk.
   B.   The effect of a declaration of a local disaster emergency is to
activate the response and recovery aspects of the village's disaster
preparedness plan of any and all applicable local or mutual aid disaster plans
and to authorize the furnishing of aid and assistance thereunder.
   C.   No mutual aid agency or official thereof may declare a local disaster
emergency, unless expressly authorized by the agreement pursuant to which the
agency functions. However, a mutual aid disaster agency shall provide aid and
services in accordance with the agreement pursuant to which it functions. (Ord.
2011-03-07, 3-7-2011)
5-7-16: EMERGENCY OPERATIONS CENTER:
The village board of trustees is authorized to designate space within the
village municipal building, or elsewhere, as needed for the safety and
effectiveness of the general staff members and responders and management of the
response and recovery of the village disaster preparedness plan and the
emergency operations center. (Ord. 2011-03-07, 3-7-2011)

Except insofar as the application thereof is clearly impractical or
inappropriate, in view of the context of purposes or penalty as provided, all
of the definitions, requirements, regulations, prohibitions, provisions and
sections of the Illinois vehicle code, 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/1-100
et seq., as amended, are hereby adopted by the village. Any and all violations
thereof shall be considered violations of this title. (Ord. 2010-1, 3-1-2010)
6-1-2: SPEED LIMIT:
No person shall drive or operate a motor vehicle upon any public street or
alley in the village at a speed in excess of twenty (20) miles per hour.

6-1-6: PARKING AND LOADING RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   No Parking Streets: The following are designated no parking areas and
no parking signs shall be placed at the appropriate locations:
 
Location
Dead end at 318 Logan Street
South side of Jones Street from the middle school to Illinois Route 94
 
   B.   Angle Parking On Certain Streets: It shall be unlawful for any person
to leave any motor vehicle parked on Broadway Street between Nichols Street and
the Atchison, Topeka and Santa Fe Railway unless said vehicle is parked at the
side of the street at an angle of about forty five degrees (45°) to the curb,
the right side of the vehicle being nearest the curb.
   C.   Time Limit Parking: It shall be unlawful for any person to park a
vehicle on the following streets for a period exceeding twenty four (24)
continuous hours; provided, however, it shall be unlawful for any person
engaged in a business in the village to park a vehicle on the following
described portions of the streets in the village for a period exceeding five
(5) successive hours:
Broadway Street between its intersection with the Atchison, Topeka and Santa Fe
Railroad and the intersection of Broadway Street with Dixon Street.
Main Street between its intersection with Division Street and the intersection
of Main Street with State Bond Issue Route 94.
Nichols Street and its intersection with Mary Street.
   D.   Parking Farm Vehicles And Vehicles With Excess Length: It shall be
unlawful for any motor vehicle with an overall length, including load,
exceeding twenty feet (20'), or any farm implement to be parked on the
following streets in the village:
The portion of Broadway Street between the Atchison, Topeka and Santa Fe
Railroad and the intersection of Broadway Street with Nichols Street.
   E.   Bus Loading And Student Drop Off/Pick Up Zones: The following are bus
loading and student drop off/pick up zones in the village:
South Street: The south curb line of South Street in front of the school near
the semicircle drive is a bus loading zone. The zone shall run approximately
fifty five feet (55') west from the crosswalk and stop ten feet (10') east of
the fire hydrant located on the corner of the semicircle drive. The student
drop off/pick up zone shall run approximately one hundred forty feet (140')
north of the crosswalk to the alley on the south curb line of South Street.
(Ord. 2010-1, 3-1-2010)
   F.   Handicapped Parking Spaces:
      1.   The first two (2) available spaces south of the west driveway of
Fisher's Food Center at approximately 109 South Broadway on the east side of
Broadway Street in the village of Stronghurst is hereby designated as
handicapped person parking only.
      2.   The parking space centered in front of the Antiquity at 113 South
Broadway and Bygones & Buds at 115 South Broadway on the east side of Broadway
Street in the village of Stronghurst is hereby designated as handicapped person
parking only.
      3.   The village clerk is requested to notify the superintendent of
streets of this designation, and the superintendent of streets shall thereupon
place an appropriate sign at such locations, noting that such spaces are
parking for a designated handicapped person or persons only. No person not
possessing a village or state sticker or license authorizing them to park in
handicapped person parking, properly affixed to their vehicle, shall park in
such spaces.
      4.   Any person, firm or corporation who shall violate any provisions of
this subsection F shall be subject to punishment by a fine of seventy five
dollars ($75.00). (Ord. 2007-0108, 1-8-2007; amd. Ord. 2010-1, 3-1-2010)

                       distance 75 feet)
 
(Ord. 2010-1, 3-1-2010)
6-1-8: U-TURNS:
   A.   Vehicles crossing from one side of the street to the other shall do so
by turning to left so as to head in the same direction as the traffic on that
side of the street toward which the crossing is made, and when the street is
congested with traffic, such vehicles shall go to the intersection before
turning.
   B.   It shall be unlawful for any motor vehicle on Broadway Street in the
village between Nichols Street and the right of way of the Atchison, Topeka and
Santa Fe Railroad to enter a parking area on the side of the street in the
opposite lane without first entering an intersection and making a U-turn in
order to reverse the direction of said vehicle. No vehicle shall enter a
parking space adjacent to the opposite lane of traffic of said vehicle. For the
purposes of this subsection, entry into a parking space by a vehicle on the
side of the street opposite the lane of traffic of said vehicle shall be
construed as an illegal turn. No vehicle shall back into an intersection.
   C.   U-turns shall be permitted at the following intersections:
      Main Street and Broadway Street.
      Nichols Street and Broadway Street.
      The right of way of the Atchison, Topeka and Santa Fe Railroad on
Broadway Street. (Ord. 2010-1, 3-1-2010)
6-1-9: NO U-TURNS:
 
Street Intersection   Direction Of Travel
Broadway/South Street South
 
(Ord. 2010-1, 3-1-2010)
6-1-10: RIDING ON, DRIVING ON, AND OBSTRUCTING SIDEWALKS:
No person shall lead, ride or drive or place any beast of burden or other
animal or any vehicle on any sidewalk or footpath otherwise than in going into
or out of premises owned by himself or his employer, nor in any manner injure
or destroy or unnecessarily obstruct the same. (Ord. 2010-1, 3-1-2010)
6-1-11: ENFORCEMENT:
Violations of this chapter may be enforced as outlined under the Illinois
vehicle code or as a village ordinance citation for nonmoving violations only
as outlined in the Illinois vehicle code. It shall be at the discretion of the
arresting officer to enter the violation as an ordinance violation or as a
violation of the Illinois vehicle code. Violations of this chapter will have a
minimum fine of not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) for the first offense and
may be increased in twenty five dollar ($25.00) increments for repeated
violations. The violator may plead "guilty" for the issued ordinance violation
and may pay the fine in person or by mail to the office of the village clerk by
the "fines due date" as indicated on the ordinance citation. The violator may
plead "not guilty" and request a court hearing to be scheduled at the Henderson
County courthouse. Such requests shall be submitted by the "fines due date". At
that time the violator shall be notified by mail of the scheduled court date.
Pending disposition of the court's ruling, the violator shall be subject to the
original fine and/or all court costs including all village attorney fees. (Ord.
2010-1, 3-1-2010)
CHAPTER 2
VEHICLE TOWING AND IMPOUND
SECTION:
6-2-1: Definitions
6-2-2: Violations Authorizing Impound

6-2-1: DEFINITIONS:
   BUSINESS DAY: Days and hours of operation as posted in front of municipal
building.
   LEVEL 1 ADMINISTRATIVE FEE: Fine, cost, or bond of impound shall be five
hundred dollars ($500.00).
   LEVEL 2 ADMINISTRATIVE FEE: Fine, cost, or bond of impound shall be two
hundred fifty dollars ($250.00).
   MOTOR VEHICLE: Every vehicle that is self-propelled, including, but not
limited to, automobiles, trucks, vans, motorcycles, ATVs, scooters, watercraft,
farm vehicles and/or may include equipment trailers.
   OWNER OF RECORD: The record titleholder(s) of motor vehicle as registered
with the Illinois secretary of state, state of Illinois; or if not registered
in Illinois, the particular state where the motor vehicle is registered. If the
owner of record can not be positively identified, the operator of the motor
vehicle will be therefore considered as the "owner of record" until the titled
holder is positively identified.
   TOW-STORAGE FEE: Fee that may be charged by the tow or storage company for
tow, removal and/or storage of vehicle. This fee shall be considered separate
and in addition to any administrative fees, fines or incarceration responsible
to the owner of record. (Ord. 2010-11-01, 11-1-2010)
6-2-2: VIOLATIONS AUTHORIZING IMPOUND:
   A.   The provisions of this chapter shall be in addition to and shall not
replace or otherwise abrogate any existing state or federal law or village
ordinance that relates to the seizure and/or impoundment of motor vehicles, and
any penalty provided herein shall be in addition to any and all penalties that
may be assessed or imposed by a court for violation of any criminal offense or
local ordinance violation offense.
   B.   Any motor vehicle, operated/possessed by the owner of record or with
the express or implied permission of the owner of record, that is used in
connection with the following violations, including all issued state and
federal warrants for arrest, shall be subject to seizure and impoundment by the
village of Stronghurst, and the owner of record of said motor vehicle, shall be
liable to the village for a level 1 administrative fee ($500.00), as provided
for in this chapter, in addition to any additional fines, court fees,
incarceration, towing and storage fees as hereinafter provided.

6-2-3: SEIZURE AND IMPOUND:
   A.   Whenever a police officer has reason to believe that a motor vehicle is
subject to seizure and impoundment pursuant to this chapter, the police officer
shall provide for the towing of the motor vehicle to an approved facility by
the village. This may include removing the motor vehicle from the scene of the
arrest by a police officer and stored on village property. In this
circumstance, the owner of record shall not be charged a "towing or storage"
fee. This chapter shall not apply if the motor vehicle used in the violation
was stolen at the time and the theft was reported to the appropriate police
authorities within twenty four (24) hours after the theft was discovered or
reasonably should have been discovered.
   B.   The police officer shall notify any person identifying him or herself
as the owner of the motor vehicle or any person who is found to be in control
of the motor vehicle at the time of the alleged violation, if there is such a
person, of the fact of the seizure and impoundment of the motor vehicle and of
the owner of record's right to request an administrative hearing to be
conducted under this chapter. (Ord. 2010-11-01, 11-1-2010)
6-2-4: ADMINISTRATIVE HEARING:
   A.   Within five (5) business days after a motor vehicle is seized and
impounded pursuant to this chapter, the village shall notify by personal
service or by certified mail to the owner of record of the owner's right to
request a hearing to challenge whether a violation of this chapter has
occurred. The owner of record seeking a hearing must file a written request for
a hearing with the chief of police, or his designee, no later than ten (10)
business days after notice was mailed. The hearing date must be scheduled no
more than twenty (20) business days after the request for a hearing has been
filed. All interested persons shall be given a reasonable opportunity to be
heard at the hearing. The formal rules of evidence shall not apply at the
hearing and hearsay evidence shall be admissible.
   B.   If, after the hearing, the hearing officer determines by a
preponderance of the evidence that the motor vehicle was used in violation of
this chapter, then the hearing officer shall enter an order finding the owner
of record of the motor vehicle liable to the village for the applicable
administrative fee.
   C.   If, after a hearing, the hearing officer does not determine by a
preponderance of the evidence that the motor vehicle was used in such a
violation, the hearing officer shall enter an order finding for the owner and
for the return of the motor vehicle.
   D.   If the owner of record requests a hearing but fails to appear at the
hearing or fails to request a hearing in a timely manner, the owner of record
shall be deemed to have waived his or her right to a hearing and the hearing
officer shall enter a default order in favor of the village in the amount of
the administrative fee. However, if the owner of record pays such
administrative fee and the motor vehicle is returned to the owner, no default
order need be entered if the owner is informed of his or her right to a hearing
and signs a written waiver, in which case an order of liability shall be deemed
to have been made when the village receives the written waiver.
   E.   If a bond in the amount equal to the applicable administrative fee is
posted with the police department, the impounded motor vehicle shall be
released to the owner of record. The owner of the motor vehicle shall still be
liable to the towing agent for any applicable towing fees.
   F.   If an administrative fee is imposed for a violation of this chapter,
the bond will be forfeited to the village; however if a violation of this
chapter is not proven by preponderance of the evidence, the bond will be
returned to the person posting the bond. All bond money posted pursuant to this
chapter shall be held by the village until the hearing officer issues a
decision, or, if there is a judicial review, until the court of jurisdiction
issues its orders.
   G.   Any party aggrieved by a final decision of the hearing officer may
appeal that decision pursuant to any applicable statutes or procedures under
the laws of the state of Illinois. (Ord. 2010-11-01, 11-1-2010)
6-2-5: DISPOSITION OF IMPOUNDED MOTOR VEHICLE:
An administrative fee imposed pursuant to this chapter shall constitute a debt
due and owing the village. A motor vehicle impounded pursuant to this chapter
shall remain impounded until:
   A.   The administrative fee is paid to the village and all applicable towing
and storage fees are paid to the towing agent, in which case the owner of
record shall be given possession of the motor vehicle; or
   B.   A bond in an amount equal to the applicable administrative fee is
posted with the police department and all applicable towing fees are paid to
the towing agent, at which time the motor vehicle will be released to the owner
of record; or
   C.   The motor vehicle is deemed abandoned in which case the motor vehicle
shall be disposed of in the manner provided by law for the disposition of
abandoned motor vehicles. (Ord. 2010-11-01, 11-1-2010)
6-2-6: MOTOR VEHICLE POSSESSION:
Any motor vehicle that is not reclaimed within thirty (30) days after the
expiration of the time during which the owner of record may seek judicial
review of the village's action under this chapter, or the time at which a final
judgment is rendered against an owner of record who is in default, may be
disposed of as an unclaimed motor vehicle as provided by law, provided,
however, that where proceedings have been instituted under state or federal
drug asset forfeiture laws, the subject motor vehicle may not be disposed of by
the village except as consistent with those proceedings. (Ord. 2010-11-01, 11-
1-2010)
6-2-7: TOWING AGENCY:
   A.   It shall be the duty of the towing or storage company in possession of
the motor vehicle to obtain documentation issued by the police department
confirming compliance with foregoing requirements, and retain photocopies of
that documentation in their files for a period of not less than six (6) months
following release of the motor vehicle. The foregoing information shall be made
available to the authorities of the village of Stronghurst for inspection and
copying, upon their request, by the towing or storage company. The towing or
storage company is prohibited from releasing any motor vehicle they may tow
from within the village involving the police department until directed by a
representative of the department and/or unless they obtain documentation as
aforesaid.
   B.   The towing or storage company shall be entitled to receive a reasonable
fee from the owner or person entitled to possession of any such motor vehicle
prior to the release of the motor vehicle. The fee shall be to cover the cost
of removing said motor vehicle and, in addition thereto, the cost of storage of
said motor vehicle for each day or fraction thereof that said motor vehicle
shall have remained stored.
   C.   The fees in this section shall be in addition to any fee levied or
assessed against the owner or operator of said motor vehicle by reason of
violation of any ordinance or statute and any arrest which may have resulted
from such violation. (Ord. 2010-11-01, 11-1-2010)
6-2-8: REFUND OF ADMINISTRATIVE FEE:
In the event a judgment of not guilty is entered by a court of competent
jurisdiction on all underlying charges that could have resulted in the
impoundment of a motor vehicle, then upon within thirty (30) days of
presentation of a certified copy of said judgment to the village police
department, any administrative fees or posted bonds obtained by the village
shall be refunded to the paying party. The village is not responsible for the
refund of any/all towing and/or storage fees. (Ord. 2010-11-01, 11-1-2010)
CHAPTER 3
OPERATION OF NONHIGHWAY VEHICLES
SECTION:
6-3-1: Definitions
6-3-2: Specifications
6-3-3: Minimum Vehicle Requirements
6-3-4: Vehicle Inspection For Approved Use
6-3-1: DEFINITIONS:
   GOLF CART: A vehicle specifically designed and intended for the purposes of
transporting one or more persons and their golf clubs or maintenance equipment
while engaged in the playing of golf, supervising the play of golf, or
maintaining the condition of the grounds on a public or private golf course.
   NEIGHBORHOOD VEHICLE: A self-propelled, electric powered, four (4) wheeled
motor vehicle (or a self-propelled, gasoline powered, 4 wheeled motor vehicle
with an engine displacement under 1,200 cubic centimeters) that is capable of
attaining in one mile a speed of more than twenty (20) miles per hour, but not
more than twenty five (25) miles per hour, and which does not conform to
federal regulations under title 49 CFR part 571.500.
   RECREATIONAL OFF HIGHWAY VEHICLE: Any motorized off highway device designed
to travel primarily off highway, sixty four inches (64") or less in width,
having a manufacturer's dry weight of two thousand (2,000) pounds or less,
traveling on four (4) or more nonhighway tires, designed with a nonstraddle
seat and a steering wheel for steering control, except equipment such as lawn
mowers. (Ord. 2011-06-06, 6-6-2011; amd. Ord. 2017-01-02, 1-2-2017)
6-3-2: SPECIFICATIONS:
   A.   The village of Stronghurst, through enforcement through the Stronghurst
police department, may restrict the types of nonhighway vehicles that are
authorized for use on village streets, alleys, and/or roadways.
   B.   Nonhighway vehicles are subject to the same speed limits and traffic
regulations as normal motor vehicles.
   C.   Operators of nonhighway vehicles must have a valid state issued
driver's license.
   D.   Operators of nonhighway vehicles may not cross Illinois Route 94.
   E.   This chapter does not include vehicles used and/or considered as
neighborhood vehicles, off highway, recreational off highway vehicles, and/or
farm related vehicles except as outlined under 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes
5/11. (Ord. 2011-06-06, 6-6-2011)
6-3-3: MINIMUM VEHICLE REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Minimum vehicle requirements include the following:
   Brake lights
   Brakes
   Headlight (visible 500 feet)
   Rearview mirror
   Red reflectorized warning devices in front and rear
   Red taillight (visible 100 feet)
   Steering apparatus
   Turn signals
   B.   Headlights and taillights are required to be on during use.
   C.   All nonhighway vehicles are subject to mandatory insurance requirements
(either auto or home policy). (Ord. 2011-06-06, 6-6-2011)
6-3-4: VEHICLE INSPECTION FOR APPROVED USE:
   A.   All nonhighway vehicles must be inspected by the Stronghurst police
department certifying that the vehicle has met all minimum requirements prior
to use on village streets, alleys and/or roadways.
   B.   Once approved, the nonhighway vehicle will be issued a sticker that
must be clearly displayed at all times during operation while the nonhighway
vehicle inspection sheet shall remain on file with the Stronghurst police
department.
All other specifications and/or requirements not included or covered under this
chapter shall be governed as outlined under 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/
11-1426.1. (Ord. 2011-06-06, 6-6-2011)
TITLE 7
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND PUBLIC WAYS
SECTION:
7-1-1: Street Grade
7-1-2: Compliance With State Law
7-1-3: Procedure To Establish, Alter Or Vacate Streets
7-1-4: Sidewalk Construction And Repair
7-1-5: Excavations
7-1-6: Culverts
7-1-7: Damage To Streets Prohibited
7-1-8: Ice And Snow Removal Required
7-1-1: STREET GRADE:
The survey made by Thomas McClanahan, a civil engineer under the laws of
Illinois in 1895, of the streets of the village and the grade established by
him in said survey, according to the profile and field notes now on file in the
office of the village clerk, is hereby adopted as the grade for streets of the
village and streets abutting thereto. All plats of property in effect at the
effective date hereof are hereby readopted as official plats. (1993 Code p. 60
§ 403.3-16)
7-1-2: COMPLIANCE WITH STATE LAW:
In all matters pertaining to the laying out of the streets, alleys and highways
in the village, when not otherwise provided by ordinance, the laws of the state
of Illinois relating to the laying out of roads and applicable to counties not
under township organization shall apply. (1993 Code p. 60 § 403.3-15)
7-1-3: PROCEDURE TO ESTABLISH, ALTER OR VACATE STREETS:
   A.   Petition Required: The village board of trustees may alter, widen or
vacate any street, alley or highway, or lay out any new street, alley or
highway within the corporate limits of the village when petitioned by any
number of freeholders, not less than twelve (12), residing within the village.
(1993 Code p. 58 § 403.3-3)
   B.   Contents Of Petition: Said petition shall set forth, in writing, the
description of the street, alley or highway, and what part thereof is to be
altered, widened or vacated; and if for a new street, alley or highway, the
names of the owners of the land, if known, and if not known, it shall be so
stated, over which the street, alley or highway is to pass; the points at which
it is to commence; its general course; and the place at or near which it is to
terminate. (1993 Code p. 58 § 403.3-4)
   C.   Meeting To Consider Action: Whenever the board of trustees shall
receive any such petition as in subsections A and B of this section specified,
they shall fix a time when and a place where they will meet to examine the
route of said street, alley or highway, and hear reasons for and against the
altering, widening, vacating, or laying out the same; and they shall give at
