10-1-2: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
The provisions of this title shall be applied in the following manner:
   A.   The provisions this Title shall apply to the entire Village of
Stronghurst (“Village”) and that area within one and one-half (1-1/2) miles of
the corporate limits.
   B.   Nothing contained in this title shall impose restrictions with respect
to land used or to be used for agricultural purposes or with respect to the
erection, maintenance, repair, alteration, remodeling, or extension of
buildings or structures used or to be used for agricultural purposes, but said
buildings shall conform to building or setback lines, and a building permit
with respect to land used for agricultural purposes and buildings thereon may
be required.
   C.   Nothing contained in this title shall impose restrictions or
regulations regarding the type or location of any poles, towers, wires, cables,
conduits, vaults, laterals, or any other similar distributing equipment of a
“public utility” as defined by Illinois law.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. 2006 Code;
Ord. 07December2020, 12-7-2020)
10-1-3: PROHIBITED BUILDING:
No structure or improvement shall be built, modified, or adjusted in a manner
which would violate any of the provisions of this Title.  (Ord. 07December2020,
12-7-2020)
10-1-4: SEPARABILITY:
If any portion of this title is, for any reason, held to be invalid by a court
of competent jurisdiction, such decision shall not affect the validity of this
title as a whole or any part thereof other than that part so declared to be
invalid. (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December2020, 12-7-2020)
10-1-5: ORDER OF BUILDING; ACCESSORY BUILDINGS:
No accessory building shall be constructed upon a lot until the construction of
the main building has been actually commenced, and no accessory building shall
be used for dwelling purposes unless the main building on the lot is also being
used for dwelling purposes.  (Ord. 07December2020, 12-7-2020)
10-1-6: STORAGE/SHIPPING CONTAINERS:
The regulation of temporary and permanent storage units/shipping containers
shall be controlled and shall confirm to the regulations prescribed in this
section, and shall meet the specific regulations prescribed in this section,
and shall meet the specifications as required in each zoning district.
   A.   Storage/shipping container means a unit originally or specifically
designed or used to store goods or merchandise during shipping or hauling by
container ships, rail, or other types of transportation.
   B.   For the purpose of this section, cargo containers, railroad cars, truck
vans, converted mobile homes, trailers, recreational vehicles, bus bodies,
vehicles and similar prefabricated items and structures originally built for
purposes other than the storage of goods and materials, are not accessory
storage buildings.
   C.   At no time shall any temporary or permanent storage/shipping containers
be placed in any districts of the Village of Stronghurst, Illinois until a
permit has been approved by the Zoning Committee.
   D.   Temporary use: storage/shipping containers shall be allowed as a
temporary use within the Village of Stronghurst in the following instances:
      1.   A building permit is required for any storage/shipping containers
being set or put in place at any location in the Village of Stronghurst.
      2.   Only one storage/shipping container is allowed on any property.
      3.   Only storage/shipping containers twenty (20) foot and less in length
are allowed.
      4.   A limit of one permit per calendar year shall be granted for a
maximum of thirty (30) days, with one thirty (30) day extension possible at the
discretion of the Zoning Committee.
      5.   Placement of the temporary storage/shipping containers must be
approved by the zoning committee.
      6.   For short-term storage of goods of business enterprises located
within a district zoned for business, light industrial, or heavy industrial
(for example: holiday season for storage).
      7.   No stacking of material on top of the storage/shipping container is
allowed.
      8.   All temporary storage/shipping containers must meet the established
setbacks for any districts in the Village of Stronghurst.
      9.   At a construction site for the duration of the project, with the
containers to be removed within thirty (30) days of the completion of the
project.
      10.   Storage/shipping containers shall be allowed as a temporary use
within the village in a residential zone for a period not to exceed ten (10)
days, such units shall only be for the use of persons utilizing the units as
PODS (Portable on Demand Storage) for moving and/or temporary storage. A
temporary building permit will be required for the storage/shipping container
to be used for a time period not to exceed ten (10) days, when using as a
moving or temporary storage container.
   E.   Permanent use: storage/shipping containers shall be allowed as a
permanent use within the Village of Stronghurst only under the following
instances:
      1.   Containers shall be allowed as an accessory use only and subject to
the requirements of the zoning district in which it is located.
      2.   A building permit is required for any storage/shipping containers
being set or put in place at any location in the Village of Stronghurst.
      3.   Only one storage/shipping container is allowed on any property.
      4.   Placement of the permanent storage/shipping containers must be
approved by the Zoning Committee.
      5.   At no time shall any permanent storage/shipping container be allowed
to be placed anywhere other than in the rear yard.
      6.   Only storage/shipping containers twenty (20) foot and less in length
are allowed.
      7.   All signage on the container shall be removed and the container
shall be painted an earth tone color or a color of siding material compatible
with the surrounding environment or adjacent structures. The painting or siding
shall be completed within thirty (30) days of the placement of the container.
This provision shall apply retroactively; therefore, all permanent use storage/
shipping containers, whenever placed, including before the adoption of this
chapter, shall be required to comply with this provision regarding signage and
painting.
      8.   No stacking of material on top of the storage/shipping container is
allowed. This provision shall apply retroactively; therefore, all permanent use
storage/shipping containers, whenever placed, including before the adoption of
this chapter, shall be required to comply with this provision regarding
stacking of materials on such storage/shipping containers.
      9.   The container shall be safe, structurally sound, and be placed on a
stable surface.
      10.   Any container that becomes unsafe, unstable, or dangerous, as
determined by the Zoning Committee, shall be removed or repaired immediately by
the property owner.
      11.   All permanent use containers shall be anchored or otherwise secured
to some stable surface.
      12.   Containers shall not be stored in a manner that impedes access to
public right-of-way, public utilities, drainage easements, adjacent structures
or buildings.
      13.   No containers may be utilized as rental units or be leased to
anyone other than the property owner or business where container is placed.
      14.   Containers shall not be connected to utility services, with the
exception of electricity, nor shall any other utility service be utilized
within the container.
      15.   All storage/shipping containers are subject to inspection of
contents to ensure adherence to the ordinance as set forth.  (Ord.
07December2020, 12-7-2020)
CHAPTER 2
ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT
SECTION:
10-2-1: Enforcement Official
10-2-2: Zoning Committee
10-2-3: Building Permit
10-2-4: Procedure For Building Permit Issuance
10-2-5: Variances
10-2-6: Expiration Of Building Permits
10-2-7: Amendments
10-2-8: Violation; Penalties
10-2-1: ENFORCEMENT OFFICIAL:
It shall be the duty of the Zoning Chairman, along with the Police Department,
to enforce the provisions of all Zoning Ordinances.
   A.   In the case of any building or structure erected, constructed,
reconstructed, altered, repaired, converted, or maintained in violation of the
provisions of these Zoning Regulations, the Village Attorney, in addition to
any other remedies available under these Zoning Regulations, is hereby
authorized to institute an action to enjoin, or any other appropriate action or
proceeding to prevent or correct such erection, construction, reconstruction,
alteration, repair, conversion, maintenance, or use.
   B.   In the case of any persons violating any provision of the zoning
ordinances the following protocol shall be followed by the Zoning Chairman:
      1.   Building Without an Approved Building Permit. Zoning Chairman shall
contact persons and inform them that they are in violation of the Village of
Stronghurst Zoning Ordinance and:
         a.   Zoning Chairman shall inform violators that any and all work at
the said property must cease until a building permit has been approved by the
zoning committee.
         b.   Zoning Chairman shall take building permit to or inform violators
that a building permit may be picked up at Stronghurst Village Hall.
         c.   If violators continue to build without the approved building
permit the Zoning Chairman shall contact and turn matter over to the Village of
Stronghurst Attorney.
      2.   Violating an Approved Building Permit. Zoning Chairman shall contact
persons and inform them that they are in violation of the Village of
Stronghurst Zoning Ordinances and inform them that if not resolved within
thirty (30) days the matter will be turned over to the Village of Stronghurst
Attorney.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. 2006 Code; Ord. 07December2020, 12-7-2020)
10-2-2: ZONING COMMITTEE:
The Zoning Committee shall be made up of at least four (4) members, appointed
annually by the President of the Board of Trustees of the Village of
Stronghurst, and shall be comprised of an equal number of Board members and
citizens of the Village.  (Ord. 07December2020, 12-7-2020)
10-2-3: BUILDING PERMIT 1 :
Building permits shall be required for any building or structure over one
hundred (100) square feet subject to the following provisions:
   A.   Nonagricultural Buildings: No nonagricultural building or structure
shall be erected, added to, or structurally altered until a Building Permit has
been issued by the Zoning Committee or Board of Trustees of the Village of
Stronghurst. Except upon a written order of the Zoning Committee or Board of
Trustees, no such Building Permit shall be issued for any building where said
construction, addition, alteration, or use thereof would be in violation of any
of the provisions of this title.
   B.   Agricultural Buildings: No agricultural building or structures
exceeding one thousand dollars ($1,000) in total cost shall be erected, added
to, or structurally altered until a building permit has been issued by the
Zoning Committee or Board of Trustees of the Village of Stronghurst.
   C.   Any temporary or moveable building or structure, including, but not
limited to, "skid" style buildings or structures, shall require a building
permit, and shall not be excused from the requirement of receiving a building
permit before placement or erection by their temporary or removable nature. 
(Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December2020, 12-7-2020)
 
Notes
1    See also section
  9-1-2 of this code.
10-2-4: PROCEDURE FOR BUILDING PERMIT ISSUANCE:
The procedure for the issuance of all building permits shall be as follows:
   A.   Application for building permit. The application for building permit
shall be kept at the office of the Village Clerk and made conveniently
available for applicants. Each applicant is hereby required to fully complete
an application for building permit, and return such completed application to
the Village Clerk for processing.
   B.   Submission to Zoning Committee. Upon receipt of a completed application
for building permit, the Village Clerk shall send notice and a copy of the
Application to each member of the Zoning Committee for review.
   C.   Vote by Zoning Committee. Within thirty (30) days of receipt of an
application for building permit by the Village Clerk, the Zoning Committee
shall discuss the application, vote on whether to approve or deny a building
permit to the applicant, and shall notify the Village Clerk of their decision.
The applicant may be present for this meeting.
   D.   Notification and issuance of building permit. Within five (5) days of
the Village Clerk's receipt of the Zoning Committee's decision regarding an
individual application for building permit, the Village Clerk shall notify the
applicant of the Zoning Committee's decision. If the Zoning Committee has
approved the application, the Village Clerk shall immediately issue a building
permit to the applicant.
   E.   Appeals to the Board of Trustees. Within thirty (30) days of the
Village Clerk's notification that the Zoning Committee has denied an
application for building permit and refused to issue a building permit, the
applicant may, by requesting in any written document delivered to the Village
Clerk within the time frame contained herein, appeal the decision of the Zoning
Committee to the Board of Trustees of the Village of Stronghurst.  (Ord.
07December2020, 12-7-2020)
10-2-5: VARIANCES:
Variances shall be requested, approved, and issued pursuant to the terms
governing the issuance of building permits, except that the timelines contained
in such terms shall not be applied to variance applications. Should a variance
be requested, it shall be clearly marked as a variance on the application for
building permit.  (Ord. 07December2020, 12-7-2020)
10-2-6: EXPIRATION OF BUILDING PERMITS:
All building permits shall be valid for a period of six (6) months from the
date of issuance. The project approved in the building permit must be started
before the deadline of this expiration period; if the project is not started
within this period, a new building permit must be issued pursuant to the
procedure contained herein.  (Or8d. 07December2020, 12-7-2020)
10-2-7: AMENDMENTS:
The corporate authorities may, from time to time, amend, supplement, change,
modify, or repeal this Title, in part or in full, pursuant to their authority.
(Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. 2006 Code; Ord. 07December2020, 12-7-2020)
10-2-8: VIOLATION; PENALTIES:
The owner or resident of any building, structure, or land in or upon which a
violation of this Title exists shall be in violation of this ordinance and
subject to a fine not to exceed seven hundred and fifty dollars ($750). A
separate offense shall be deemed committed on each day that such violation
occurs or continues. (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. 2006 Code; Ord. 07December2020, 12-
7-2020)
CHAPTER 3
ZONING DISTRICTS AND MAP
SECTION:
10-3-1: Zoning Districts Established
10-3-2: Zoning District Map
10-3-3: Amending Zoning Districts
10-3-4: Zoning Of Vacated Areas
10-3-1: ZONING DISTRICTS ESTABLISHED:
The village, and the area within one and one-half (1-1/2) miles of the
corporate limits of the village, shall be classified and divided into five (5)
districts. These districts shall be designated as follows:
   Agricultural District:  A-1.
   Dwelling District:  R-1 and R-2.
   Business District:  B-1.
   Industrial District: I-1.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. 2006 Code; Ord.
07December2020, 12-7-2020)
10-3-2: ZONING DISTRICT MAP:
A map indicating the various zoning districts in the Village shall be kept at
the office of the Village Clerk and made conveniently available for public
inspection. (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. 2006 Code; Ord. 07December2020, 12-7-2020)
10-3-3: AMENDING ZONING DISTRICTS:
Zoning districts may be changed, altered, or otherwise amended by the Board of
Trustees of the Village of Stronghurst.  (Ord.  07 December2020, 12-7-2020)
10-3-4: ZONING OF VACATED AREAS:
Whenever any street, alley, or other area is vacated by proper authority, the
districts adjoining such vacated property shall be extended automatically to
the center of such vacated property, and all area included in the vacated
property shall then and henceforth be subject to all appropriate regulations of
the extended districts.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December2020, 12-7-2020)
CHAPTER 4
A-1 AGRICULTURAL DISTRICT
SECTION:
10-4-1: Scope
10-4-2: Permitted Uses
10-4-3: Building Height
10-4-4: Lot Area
10-4-5: Yards
10-4-6: Off Street Parking Facilities
10-4-1: SCOPE:
Within the A-1 Agricultural District, the regulations of this chapter shall
apply.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December2020, 12-7-2020)
10-4-2: PERMITTED USES:
"Accessory use of building," as defined in subsection
10-1-2B of this Title and as regulated by Section
10-1-6 of this Title, including the following accessory uses:
   Buildings and structures accessory to agricultural uses, including roadside
stands selling produce grown on the premises; provided, that such stands are
located not less than fifty feet (50') from a street or highway right of way.
Agricultural and agricultural buildings; provided, that no livestock is housed
closer than four hundred feet (400') from any lot in any R District.
Billboards and signboards subject to the following restrictions:
   A.   No billboard or signboard shall be located within four hundred feet
(400') of any R  District.
   B.   Billboards or signboards may have constant or flashing illumination;
provided, that any such sign located in the direct line of vision of any
traffic control signaling device shall not have contrasting or flashing
intermittent illumination of red, greed, or amber color.  Where a sign is
illuminated by light reflected upon it, direct rays of light shall not project
upon any part of any existing state or federal highway right-of-way, existing
residential structure or any R District.
   C.   All billboards shall comply with the Illinois Highway Advertising
Control Act of 1971.
Buildings or structures occupied by or used for places of worship, Sunday
schools, parish houses, public and parochial schools, public libraries,
museums, and similar public cultural uses located not less than forty feet
(40') from any other side lot line in any R District.
Cemeteries.
Country clubs, golf courses, swimming clubs and similar recreational uses;
provided, that any principal or accessory building in connection therewith
shall be located not less than two hundred feet (200') from any other lot in
any R District.
"Essential services", as defined in Subsection
10-1-2B of this Title, and public service buildings or properties, except such
uses as storage yards, warehouses, garages, or other uses customarily conducted
as gainful businesses, provided any building is located not less than forty
feet (40') from any other lot in any R District.
Existing railroad rights-of-way, not including switching, storage freight yards
or sidings.
Farm dwellings and single-family non-farm dwellings.
"Home occupations", as defined in Subsection
10-1-2B of this Title.
Mobile home parks and mobile home courts.
Open air recreational use such as parks and playgrounds.
Sale of nursery and greenhouse products where production or growth of products
takes place on the premises. 
Signs, defined as follows:
   A.   Signs accessory to roadside stands shall be limited to two (2) per lot
with no sign larger than ten square feet (10) and set back thirty feet (30')
from the right-of-way. Such signs shall be less than fifteen feet (15') in
height and pertain to agricultural products offered for sale and identification
of such stand.
   B.   Real estate signs of a temporary nature, not exceeding two (2) in
number per lot, nor larger than twelve square feet (12), set back twenty feet
(20') from any highway, street or road right-of-way.
   C.   Small announcement or professional signs not exceeding four square feet
(4) in area; except, that an announcement sign or bulletin board, not over
twelve square feet (12) in area, set back twenty feet (20') from any right-of-
way, may be erected in connection with any of the permitted principal uses of a
nonresidential character.
   D.   A sign or signs flat against the building appertaining to a
nonconforming use on the premises, not exceeding in the aggregate fifty square
feet (50) in area, except as may be  authorized by the Board of Appeals.
Temporary buildings and uses for construction purposes for a period not to
exceed one year.
The following uses shall be permitted in accordance with the provisions and
procedures indicated by the governing body upon application in accordance with
and after compliance with the procedures set forth in Chapter 8 of this Title:
   Sanitary landfills in accordance with other applicable requirements and
regulations; provided, that no such landfill shall be operated within one
thousand twenty feet (1,320') of any R District.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. 2006
Code; Ord. 07December2020, 12-7-2020)
10-4-3: BUILDING HEIGHT:
There shall be no restriction on the height of buildings in agricultural
district.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December2020, 12-7-2020)
10-4-4: LOT AREA:
   A.   No lot area shall be less than one acre in size outside the Village
limits.
   B.   Public school, elementary and high, or private school having a
curriculum similar to that ordinarily given in a public elementary school or
public high school, including religious instruction in parochial schools,
hereafter erected, shall conform to the following minimum standards:
 
Elementary School: 5 acres, plus 1 acre per 100 student design capacity.
Middle School:     10 acres, plus 1 acre per 100 student design capacity.
High School:       15 acres, plus 1 acre per 100 student design capacity.
 
(Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. 2006 Code; Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-4-5: YARDS:
No minimum yard areas shall be required for agricultural use except a front
yard requirement of eighty feet (80') along state and federal highways and a
requirement of sixty feet (60') along state aid highways and other public
roads.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-4-6: OFF STREET PARKING FACILITIES:
Off street parking facilities shall be provided as required or permitted in
Chapter 9 of this Title.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-
2020)
CHAPTER 5
R-1 DWELLING DISTRICT
SECTION:
10-5-1: Scope
10-5-2: Permitted Uses
10-5-3: Building Height
10-5-4: Lot Area
10-5-5: Yards
10-5-6: Lot Coverage
10-5-7: Off Street Parking Facilities
10-5-1: SCOPE:
Within the R-1 Dwelling District, the regulations of this article shall apply.
(Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. 2006 Code; Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-5-2: PERMITTED USES:
"Accessory use or building", as defined in Subsection
10-1-2B of this Title, and as regulated by Section
10-1-6 of this Title.
Churches and similar places of worship.
Convents, monasteries, rectories or parish houses to be occupied by not more
than ten (10) persons.
Farming, truck gardening and nurseries.
"Home occupations", as defined in Subsection
10-1-2B of this Title.
Library.
Off street parking facilities, as required or permitted by Chapter 9 of this
Title.
One-family detached dwelling.
One-family row dwellings with not more than eight (8) dwelling units in one
building.
Private swimming pools appurtenant to a one-family dwelling on the same lot,
when they meet yard depth and width requirements for principal buildings in
this district, and when the swimming pool or the property on which it is
located is adequately fenced to a height of forty eight inches (48") to prevent
access of small children and meets all applicable health and sanitary
requirements.
Public school, elementary and high, or private school having a curriculum
similar to that ordinarily given in a public elementary school or public high
school, including religious instruction in parochial schools.
Signs, defined as follows:
   A.   A sign or signboard not exceeding eight square feet (8) in area,
appertaining to the sale or lease of the premises or trespassing thereon;
   B.   A nameplate not exceeding one square foot (1) in area.
   C.   A sign or bulletin board not exceeding twenty square feet (20) in area
erected upon the premises of a church or other institution for the purpose of
displaying the name and activities or services therein provided.
Temporary buildings and uses for construction purposes for a period not to
exceed one year.
Two-family dwellings and multiple dwellings not to exceed nine (9) dwelling
units or apartments per structure.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. 2006 Code; Ord.
07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-5-3: BUILDING HEIGHT:
   A.   One-family detached dwellings: Thirty feet (30'), and not over two and
one-half (2  ½) stories, except as provided in Section
10-1-6 of this Title.
   B.   Churches and similar places of worship:  Seventy-five feet (75') for
towers or steeples and not more than forty-five feet (45) for the principal
building.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-5-4: LOT AREA:
   A.   Every building hereafter erected or structurally altered as a multiple-
family dwelling or as a row house shall provide a lot area per dwelling unit of
not less than one thousand three hundred fifty square feet (1,350') and a width
at the building line of not less than fifty feet (50'), except as provided in
Section
10-1-6 of this Title.
   B.   Every one-family detached dwelling, convent, monastery, rectory or
parish house hereafter erected shall be on a lot having an area of not less
than seven thousand five hundred square feet (7,500) and a width at the
established building line of not less than fifty feet (50'), except as provided
in Section
10-1-6 of this Title.
   C.   Churches and similar places of worship hereafter erected or
structurally altered shall be on a lot having an area of not less than seven
thousand five hundred square feet (7,500), and a width at the building line of
not less than fifty feet (50').
   D.   For public and private schools, the same regulations shall apply as
required or permitted in the A-1 Agricultural District (Subsection
10-4-4B of this Title).  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-5-5: YARDS:
No building or structure shall be erected or enlarged unless the following
yards are provided and maintained in connection with such building, structure
or enlargement:
   A.   Front Yard; Each lot upon which a dwelling is constructed shall have a
front yard of not less than twenty-five feet (25') along all federal and state
rights of way and twenty feet  (20') along all others.  Where a lot has double
frontage, the required front yard shall be provided on both streets.
   B.   Side Yards:
      1.   On each lot upon which a dwelling is constructed, there shall be a
side yard on each side of not less than ten feet (10').  The combined total of
side yards for corner lots shall not be less than twenty-five feet (25').
      2.    On lots upon which a church or similar place of worship is
constructed or extension made to an existing church or a similar place of
worship, there shall be a side yard of not less than twenty feet (20') on each
side of the main structure and a combined total of side yards of not less than
forty feet (40').
   C.   Rear Yard: Every lot or parcel of land upon which a building is
constructed shall have a rear yard of not less than twenty-five feet (25'), or
twenty percent (20%) of the depth of the lot, whichever amount is larger, but
is need not exceed sixty-five feet (65').  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord.
07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-5-6: LOT COVERAGE:
All buildings, including accessory buildings, shall not cover more than thirty
percent (30%) of the area of the lot. (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December
2020, 12-7-2020)
10-5-7: OFF STREET PARKING FACILITIES:
Off street parking facilities shall be provided as required or permitted in
Chapter 9 of this Title. (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
CHAPTER 6
R-2 DWELLING DISTRICT
SECTION:
10-6-1: Permitted Uses
10-6-2: Building Height
10-6-3: Lot Area
10-6-4: Yards
10-6-5: Lot Coverage
10-6-6: Off Street Parking Facilities
10-6-1: PERMITTED USES:
Any use permitted in the R-1 Dwelling District (Section 10-5A-2 of this
Title).  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. 2006 Code; Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-6-2: BUILDING HEIGHT:
The same regulations shall apply as required or permitted in the R-1 Dwelling
District (Section
10-5-3 of this Title).  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. 2006 Code; Ord. 07December 2020,
12-7-2020)
10-6-3: LOT AREA:
   A.   Every one-family detached dwelling, convent, monastery, rectory or
parish house hereafter erected shall be on a lot having an area of not less
than fifteen thousand (15,000) square feet, and a width at the established
building line of not less than one hundred feet (100'), except as provided in
Section
10-1-6 of this Title.
   B.   Churches and similar places of worship hereafter erected or
structurally altered shall be on a lot having an area of not less than one-half
(1/2) acre and a width at the building line of not less than eighty-five feet
(85').
   C.   Regulations for public and private schools shall be the same as
required or permitted in the A-1 Agricultural District (Subsection
10-4-4B of this Title).  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-6-4: YARDS:
No building or structure shall be erected or enlarged unless the following
yards are provided and maintained in connection with such building, structure
or enlargement:
   A.   Front Yard: Each lot upon which is dwelling is constructed shall have
afront yard of not less than thirty feet (30').
   B.   Side Yards:
      1.   On each lot upon which a dwelling constructed, there shall be side
yard on each side of not less than ten feet (10'). The combined total of the
side yards for interior lots shall not be less than twenty feet (20'), and the
combined total of side yards for corner lots shall not be less than thirty feet
(30'). The side yard on each side of a building on a lot of record which is
less than seventy feet (70') in width shall have a width of not less than seven
feet (7').
      2.   On lots upon which a church or similar place of worship is
constructed or extension made to an existing church or similar place of
worship, there shall be a side yard of not less than fifteen feet (15') on each
side of the main structure and a combined total of side yards of not less than
thirty-five feet (35').
   C.   Rear Yard:  Every lot or parcel of land upon which a building is
constructed shall have a rear yard of not less than twenty-five feet (25'), or
twenty percent (20%) of the depth of the lot, whichever is larger, but it need
not exceed thirty-five feet (35').  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December 2020,
12-7-2020)
10-6-5: LOT COVERAGE:
All buildings, including accessory buildings, shall not cover more than thirty
percent (30%) of the area of the lot.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December
2020, 12-7-2020)
10-6-6: OFF STREET PARKING FACILITIES:
Parking facilities shall be provided as required or permitted in Chapter 9 of
this title. (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
CHAPTER 7
B-1 BUSINESS DISTRICT
SECTION:
10-7-1: Scope
10-7-2: Permitted Uses
10-7-3: Condition Of Use
10-7-4: Building Height
10-7-5: Yards
10-7-1: SCOPE:
Within the B-1 Business District, the regulations of this Chapter shall apply. 
(Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-7-2: PERMITTED USES:
   A.   Any use permitted in the R-2 Dwelling District (Section 10-5B-1 of this
title), except single-family dwellings.
   B.   Art, book, school supply, and stationery stores.
   Auto repair garage.
   Bakery shops, including the baking and processing of food products when
prepared for retail use on the premises only.
   Barbershop, beauty parlor, massage, or similar personal service shops.
   Candy and ice cream shop.
   Drugstores.
   Dyeing, dry cleaning, and laundry works having a boiler with a steam
generating capacity no greater than one thousand five hundred (1,500) pounds of
steam per hour, having no more than five (5) employees employed at any one time
on the premises, having a portion of the premises devoted to the pickup and
delivery to customers of items to be dyed, dry cleaned, or laundered and which
does not operate before the hour of seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. nor after the
hour of nine o'clock (9:00) P.M. and which utilizes only underwriter approved
non-flammable solutions and materials in its operations.
   Floral shop and conservatory for retail trade on the premises only.
   Food and fruit stores.
   Gift stores.
   Launderette, laundromat, or similar self-service laundry or self-service
dry-cleaning establishment.
   Meat markets.
   Newsstands.
   Rental establishments.
   Restaurant, tearoom, and café when the establishment is not of the drive-in
type where food is served to customers remaining in the motor vehicle.
   Service stations, excluding any such operation which may include the repair
or servicing of motor vehicles, except as defined under "automobile repair,
minor" in Subsection
10-1-2B of this title.
   Tobacco stores.
   Any other similar type retail stores not specifically permitted in this
subsection when authorized by the governing body after receipt of review and
recommendations from the planning commission.
   Any accessory use or building customarily incidental to the above permitted
uses and as regulated by subsequent sections of this title.
   C.   Amusement establishments: Bowling alleys, dance halls, and other
similar places of recreation when conducted wholly within a completely enclosed
building.
   Auto accessory store where there is no driveway entrance across the sidewalk
into the main building.
   Banks, financial institutions, savings and loan associations.
   Bicycle repair, sales and rental.
   Blueprinting and photo stating establishments.
   Bus passenger terminal.
   Camera and photographic supply shops for retail sales.
   Computer and office equipment sales and service.
   Custom dressmaking, millinery, tailoring or shoe repair conducted for retail
sales on the premises only.
   Department stores.
   Dry cleaning and dressing establishments, when employing facilities for the
cleaning and pressing of dry goods, received on the premises from retail trade
only and not including any wholesale cleaning or pressing business, and when
using carbon tetrachloride, perchloroethylene, or other similar non-flammable
solvents approved by the fire department.
   Dry goods store, haberdashery, and wearing apparel stores.
   Electrical appliance store and repair, but not including appliance assembly
or manufacturing.
   Frozen food lockers.
   Funeral homes and mortuaries.
   Furniture store and upholstery.
   Furrier, when conducted for retail trade on the premises only.
   Garden supplies and seed stores.
   Gift shops.
   Hardware stores.
   Hobby stores.
   Hotels, including dining and meeting rooms, when business uses occupy the
street  frontage except for an entranceway to the hotel lobby.
   Household appliance store and repair shops.
   Interior decorating shops, including upholstery and making of draperies,
slipcovers, and other similar articles, when conducted as part of the retail
operations and secondary to the main use.
   Jewelry store and watch repair.
   Leather goods and luggage store.
   Medical clinics.
   Messenger or telegraph service stations.
   Off street parking facilities in an open lot or a covered building.
   Offices, business and professional.
   Paint and wallpaper store.
   Photography studio, art gallery or studio, including the developing of film
and pictures when conducted as part of the retail business on the premises.
   Plumbing showroom, without shop or repair facilities.
   Post office.
   Public utility collection offices.
   Service stations, public garages, and other motor vehicle services, provided
no major repair work is performed out of doors, provided all pumps, underground
storage tanks, lubricating, and other devices are located at least thirty feet
(30') from any street right-of-way, provided all fuel, oil, or similar
substances are stored inside or underground, and provided all automobile parts,
dismantled vehicles, and similar articles are stored within a building.
   Shoe store.
   Sporting goods store.
   Tailor shop.
   Theaters, indoor.
   Variety store.
   Wearing apparel shop.
   Any other similar type retail store not specifically listed in this
subsection, when authorized by the governing body after receipt of review and
recommendations from the Planning Commission.
   D.   Air conditioning and heating, sales and service.
   Automobile motor repair, sales and service shop, including automobile body
repair and rebuilding, and painting of automobiles.
   Battery and the service stations.
   Beverage, non-alcoholic, bottling and distributing.
   Bicycle and motorcycle sales, repair and rental.
   Boat display, sales and service.
   Farm implement display, sales and service.
   Feed and seed store.
   Kennel.
   Mobile home sales and rental on an open lot or within a building.
   Motel.
   Pet shop or animal hospital when conducted wholly within a enclosed
building.
   Plumbing, heating, and roofing supply shops when conducted wholly within a
building.
   Recreation places, including bowling alley, dance hall, gymnasium, skating
rink, archery range, miniature golf course, or other similar places of
amusement or entertainment when operated for pecuniary profit.
   Restaurant, non-drive-in, drive-in or service.
   Uses customarily incidental to any of the uses in this subsection and
accessory buildings when located on the same premises.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd.
2006 Code; Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-7-3: CONDITION OF USE:
All activities, except for automobile off street parking, which are permitted
or required in this B-1 District shall be conducted wholly within an enclosed
building.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-7-4: BUILDING HEIGHT:
The height of all buildings or structures shall be no more than three (3)
stories or thirty-five feet (35') in height except as permitted in Section
10-1-6 of this title.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-7-5: YARDS:
No building or structure shall be constructed or enlarged unless the following
yards are provided and maintained in connection with such building:
   A.   Front Yard:
      1.   Requirements: No front yard shall be required when all frontage
between two (2) intersecting streets lies within this district.  However, when
lots within this district are adjacent to and adjoining lots in an R District,
all of which front upon the same street between two (2) intersecting streets,
there shall be established the same front yard setback for all of the frontage
as has been established in the abutting R District.
      2.   Exception:  When existing buildings located in this district have
already established a building line at the street line at a depth less than
required above, then all new buildings may conform to the same building line,
except for the first fifty feet (50') of the B-1 District frontage adjacent to
the R District, whereupon there shall be provided a front setback of not less
than ten feet (10').
   B.   Side Yards:  No side yard is required except for a corner lot which
abuts upon an R District, or upon an alley separating this district from an R
District.  There shall then be provided a side yard equal to one-half (1/2) the
front yard required in the abutting R District, but in no case more than ten
feet (10').  The same setback shall apply also if business buildings front the
intersecting street, commonly referred to as the side street.
   C.   Rear Yard:  There shall be a rear yard of not less than twenty feet
(20'); provided, however, that a one-story accessory building may be relocated
thereon, except for the five feet (5') adjacent and parallel to the rear lot
line or alley line, for the storage of motor vehicles and the unloading and
loading of vehicles under roof as provided in Chapter 9 of this title.  (Ord.,
3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
CHAPTER 8
I-1 INDUSTRIAL DISTRICT
SECTION:
10-8-1: Scope
10-8-2: Permitted Uses
10-8-3: Condition Of Use
10-8-4: Building Height
10-8-5: Yards
10-8-6: Performance Standards
10-8-7: Off Street Parking And Loading Facilities
10-8-1: SCOPE:
Within the I-1 Industrial District, the regulations of this Chapter shall
apply.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-8-2: PERMITTED USES:
An industrial use is one which creates a minimum amount of nuisance outside the
plant, and which is not noxious or offensive by reason of the emission of
smoke, dust, fumes, gas, odors, noises or vibrations beyond the confines of the
building.  The following uses are permitted in the I-1 Industrial District:
   Any agricultural use.
   Any use permitted in districts R-1, R-2, and B-1 (Sections 10-5A-2, 10-5B-
1 and
10-6-2, respectively, of this title).
   Animal hospitals.
   Bakeries.
   Bottling works.
   Building material yards where no millwork is done.
   Cabinet making establishments and carpenter shops which use no motors larger
than ten (10) horsepower.
   Clothing factories.
   Contractors' yards.
   Dairies.
   Dry cleaning plants.
   Dyeing plants.
   Feed processing and distributing facilities.
   Fruit canning and packing establishments.
   Fuel storage plants.
   Ice plants.
   Laundries.
   Machine shops.
   Manufacturing plants.
   Milk distribution stations.
   Mixing plants.
   Mobile home parks or mobile homes.
   Optical goods factories.
   Paper box factories.
   Pencil factories.
   Printing, publication, and engraving plants.
   Processing plants.
   Research and development organizations.
   Sheet metal shops.
   Storage firms.
   Trucking terminals.
   Welding shops.
   Wholesale businesses.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. 2006 Code; Ord. 07December
2020, 12-7-2020)
10-8-3: CONDITION OF USE:
The permitted uses in Section
10-8-2 of this chapter shall be subject to the following:  Any production,
processing, cleaning, servicing, testing, repair or storage of goods, materials
or products shall take place without creating disturbing influences to the use
and occupancy of adjoining properties.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December
2020, 12-7-2020)
10-8-4: BUILDING HEIGHT:
No building or structure shall exceed three (3) stories or thirty-five feet
(35') in height, except as permitted in Section
10-1-6 of this Title. (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-8-5: YARDS:
   A.   Front Yard:  All buildings and structures shall have a front yard depth
of at least ten feet (10').  Buildings and structures placed on corner lots
shall observe front yard requirements on both streets.
   B.   Side Yards:  All buildings and structures shall have side yard widths
of at least ten feet (10').
   C.   Rear Yard:  All buildings and structures shall have a rear yard depth
of at least ten feet (10').
   D.   Yards Adjacent to Residential Districts: All buildings and structures
on lots adjacent to residential districts shall be located so as to provide
side yard widths or rear yard depths of at least twenty-five feet (25')
adjacent to such residential districts.
   E.   Railroad Siding Frontage:  No yards shall be required for those
portions of lots which front on railroad sidings.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord.
07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-8-6: PERFORMANCE STANDARDS:
   A.   Noise:
      1.   The sound pressure level, to be measured as described below, shall
not exceed the following decibel levels in the designated octave bands when
adjacent to the designated types of districts.
Octave Band       Sound Level In Decibels
Cycles Per Second All Residential Districts B-1 District
0 to 75           58                        73
76 to 150         54                        69
151 to 300        50                        65
301 to 600        46                        61
601 to 1,200      40                        55
1,201 to 2,400    33                        48
2,401 to 4,800    26                        41
Over 4,800        20                        35
 
      2.   Objectionable sounds of an intermittent nature which are not easily
measured shall be controlled so as not to become a nuisance to adjacent uses.
      3.   Measurement is to be made at the nearest boundary of the nearest
residential or business area or at any other point along the boundary where the
level is higher. The sound levels shall be measured with a sound level meter
and associated octave band filter as prescribed by the American Standards
Association.
   B.   Smoke and Particulate Matter:
      1.   The emission of smoke or dusts by manufacturing plants in an amount
sufficient to create a general nuisance to adjoining properties shall be
prohibited. Total emission of smoke and particulate matter shall be limited to
the following:
   Ringelmann Requirements:  All smoke and the emission of all other
particulate matter in quantities sufficient to produce an opacity at any point
greater than Ringelmann 3 shall be prohibited. The only exception shall be a
plume consisting entirely of condensed steam. A "Ringelmann 1 unit" is defined
as twenty percent (20%) density for one minute. No more than fifteen (15) units
of Ringelmann smoke shall be permitted per hour and no smoke more intense than
Ringelmann 2; except, that during one hour of a twenty-four (24) hour day,
thirty (30) units of smoke may be emitted, but with no smoke more intense than
Ringelmann 3.
   2.   The total quantity of emitted solids shall not exceed one pound per
hour, per acre of lot area.
   C.   Odors:  No odor shall be emitted by any use permitted in this district
in such quantities as to be readily detectable by an average observer at any
point on the boundary line of the premises or beyond.
   D.   Noxious Gases:  Processes and operations of permitted uses capable of
dispersing gases or toxic particulates into the atmosphere must be hooded or
otherwise suitably enclosed. The emission of such toxic gases or particulate
matter shall be from a stack.
   E.   Glare and Heat:  Operation producing intense light or heat shall be
performed within an enclosed building and not be visible beyond any lot line
bounding the property whereon the use is conducted.
   F.   Vibrations:  No uses shall be located and no equipment shall be
installed in such a way to produce intense, earth shaking vibrations which are
noticeable at the property lines of the subject premises.  (Ord., 3-5-1973;
amd. 2006 Code; Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-8-7: OFF STREET PARKING AND LOADING FACILITIES:
Off street parking and loading facilities shall be provided as required in
Chapter 9 of this title.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
CHAPTER 9
NONCONFORMING STRUCTURES AND USES 1
SECTION:
10-9-1: Land Used For Storage; Signs
10-9-2: Continuance Of Use Of Buildings And Structures
10-9-3: Nonagricultural Buildings And Structures
10-9-4: Mobile Homes And Mobile Home Parks
10-9-5: Adjacent Small Lots
10-9-6: Abandonment Of Use
 
Notes
1    See Subsection
  10-2-3B of this title for certificate of occupancy provisions.
10-9-1: LAND USED FOR STORAGE; SIGNS:
The lawful use of land for storage purposes, except for agricultural uses or
where such use is an adjunct of any structure, and advertising signs and
bulletin boards which do not conform to the provisions of this title shall be
discontinued within one year from the effective date hereof, and the lawful use
of land for storage purposes, except for agricultural uses or where such use is
an adjunct of any structure, and signs and bulletin boards which become non-
conforming by reason of a subsequent change in this title shall also be
discontinued within one year from the date of the change. (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd.
Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-9-2: CONTINUANCE OF USE OF BUILDINGS AND STRUCTURES:
   A.   The lawful use of a building or structure existing at the effective
date hereof may be continued, although such use does not conform to the
provisions of this title.  If no structural alterations are made, a non-
conforming use of a building may be changed to another non-conforming use of
the same or of a more restricted classification.  Whenever such non-conforming
use has been changed to a more restricted use or to a conforming use, such use
shall not thereafter be changed to a less restricted use.
   B.   Whenever the lawful use of a building becomes non-conforming through a
change in zoning requirements or district boundaries, such use may be
continued, and if no structural alterations are made, it may be changed to
another non-conforming use of the same or of a more restricted classification. 
Whenever such non-conforming use has been changed to a more restricted use or
to a conforming use, such use shall not thereafter be changed to a less
restricted use.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
10-9-3: NONAGRICULTURAL BUILDINGS AND STRUCTURES:
   A.   Discontinuance of Use: Whenever a non-conforming use of a non-
agricultural building or structure, or part thereof, has been discontinued for
a period of twelve (12) consecutive months, or for a continuous period of
eighteen (18) months if the building was originally designed and constructed
for non-residential use, such use shall not, after being discontinued or
abandoned, be re-established, and the use of the premises thereafter shall be
in conformity with the regulations of the district.
   B.   Enlargement, Reconstruction, Alteration:
      1.   No existing non-agricultural building or structure devoted to a use
not permitted in the district in which such building or premises is located,
except when required to do so by law, shall be enlarged, extended,
reconstructed or structurally altered, unless such use is changed to a use
permitted in the district in which such building or structure is located;
provided, however, any building containing a residential non-conforming use may
be altered in any way to improve livability, but no structural alteration shall
be made which would increase the number of dwelling units therein or the bulk
of the building.
   C.   Damage: Any non-agricultural building or structure containing a non-
conforming use which is damaged by explosion, fire, flood, wind or other act of
nature or man of fifty percent (50%) or more of its fair market (sales value
immediately prior to damage shall not be repaired or reconstructed except in
conformity with the provisions of this title.  In the event that the building
inspector's estimate of the extent of damage or fair market value is not
acceptable to the applicant for the building permit to repair or reconstruct
such building or structure, the applicant may appeal to the Board of Appeals.
   D.   Building under Construction: Non non-agricultural building or structure
designed or intended to be utilized for a non-conforming use shall be
constructed or allowed unless substantial construction is underway at the
effective date hereof or subsequent amendment hereto and is being diligently
prosecuted so that such building or structure will be completed within eighteen
(18) months from the effective date hereof or subsequent amendment hereto.  All
outstanding building permits for construction which do not meet these
requirements shall be rendered null and void by the enactment of, or subsequent
amendment to, this tile.  (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. 2006 Code; Ord. 07December
2020, 12-7-2020)
10-9-4: MOBILE HOMES AND MOBILE HOME PARKS 1 :
   A.   Mobile Homes:  No mobile home shall be converted to a permanent
residence in R-1 and R-2 Districts.
   B.   Mobile Home Parks:  The lawful use of land as a mobile home park which
does not conform to the provisions of this title shall not be extended beyond
the area actually so used at the effective date hereof, and no new parking
spaces or berths for additional mobile homes shall be added thereto.  (Ord., 3-
5-1973; amd. 2006 Code; Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
 
Notes
1    See also title 9, chapter 2 of this code and section
  10-8-7 of this title.
10-9-5: ADJACENT SMALL LOTS:
When adjacent lots of record are in single ownership and fronting on the same
street or place, even though such lots are smaller in area and width than
permitted in the use district where located, no building or structure shall be
erected or structurally altered on such lots, except in conformity with the
provisions of this title. (Ord., 3-5-1973; amd. Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-
2020)
10-9-6: ABANDONMENT OF USE:
Where no enclosed building is involved, discontinuance of a non-conforming use
for a period of six (6) months shall constitute abandonment. (Ord., 3-5-1973;
amd. Ord. 07December 2020, 12-7-2020)
